Beijing City's New Budget Completed

(Nanjing) The Beijing Municipal Government, facing extreme financial difficulties, continues to adhere to the principle of austerity in the new budget for the 21st year, and expands operating expenses. It has now been completed and submitted to the Directorate of Budget, Accounting and Statistics for compilation as required. Regarding its contents, expenditures are concerned, administrative rules were 634,662 yuan, a decrease of 30,274 yuan compared with the previous year. If the temporary expenses of the previous year are combined, the decrease is more than 2 million yuan. In terms of operating expenses, such as education and cultural expenses and construction expenses, the actual expenditure is higher than the previous year. For example, the addition of substitute compulsory primary schools, the increase of scout troops, and the increase in the number of grades in municipal schools will increase the recurring education expenses by more than 10,000 yuan per month. The repair of roads throughout the city will increase road repair expenses by more than 10,000 yuan per month. In terms of income, it is planned to actively reorganize the existing tax revenue in order to achieve a balance between income and expenditure. (31st Central News Agency dispatch)

Central Radio Station Officially Broadcasts

(Nanjing) The 75,000-watt high-power broadcasting station prepared by the Central Government has been installed and will be used for preliminary test broadcasting this month. According to reports from various parts of the country, the reception is satisfactory. It is now scheduled to start official test broadcasting on September 1st using a wavelength of 440 meters. The original 500-watt station will be temporarily suspended for emergency use. If there is an obstruction in the high-power station, broadcasting will be carried out on a wavelength of 280 meters to compensate. The official opening date will be determined after the test is accurate. (31st Central News Agency dispatch)

Foreign Important Telegrams

Tense Situation in the Far East, Philippine Governor's Trip to the U.S. Cancelled

▲ Kuomintang News Agency, Manila, 31st - Philippine Governor-General Roosevelt, who had planned to return to the United States to participate in President Hoover's re-election campaign, suddenly announced today that his trip to the United States has been cancelled. The reason is that U.S. Secretary of War Hurley sent a telegram yesterday stating that President Hoover believes that Roosevelt urgently needs to stay in the Philippines. Therefore, Roosevelt suspended his trip to the United States. The above reasons are stated in the announcement by the Manila Governor's Office.

Answers to American Reporters' Questions During Izumi's Return Home

Actually Claims that the Eastern Provinces Are Not Chinese Territory

▲ Kuomintang News Agency, Honolulu, 30th - Japanese Ambassador to the United States, Izumi, took the Chichibu Maru from San Francisco to Yokohama. He passed through here today. According to what he told guests, the United States is now gradually understanding Japan's position in the three eastern provinces. Japan has no ambition for land in China proper. The American public has finally understood this. A guest asked if by "China proper," he was referring to the three eastern provinces. Izumi replied that [Manchukuo] is not part of China proper. The guest asked again whether Japan wants to annex [Manchukuo]. Izumi denied that Japan has this intention, but said that what can be predicted now is that Japan intends to recognize [Manchukuo] as an independent country and does not want any international objections. Izumi also denied the saying that he would permanently leave Washington, saying that he would only return home for six months. This time, he really wants to personally inspect the latest developments in the situation. Passengers on the Chichibu Maru also include movie star Fairbanks, who plans

Page 12

to go to China, Olympic athletes, and Associated Press Shanghai reporter Marshall.

German Social Democrat Elected Speaker of Parliament

Prior Agreement Reached with the Center Party Through Negotiations

Unexpectedly Quiet Opening Day

▲Berlin, National News Agency, 30th – The new parliament opened at 3 PM today. Ms. Sittkin, the eldest member of parliament from the Communist Party, presided over the session, and it proceeded peacefully, which was quite unexpected. A crowd gathered near the parliament building in the early morning to observe the arrival of the parliamentarians. Although there were no disturbances, the police began clearing the streets, forcing the onlookers to stand at a distance. Ms. Sittkin entered the parliament building through a side door sometime in the morning to avoid being swarmed by reporters, photographers, and filmmakers who were waiting for her. Members of the National Socialist Party, dressed in brown party uniforms with swastika armbands, arrived successively and quietly took their seats. Communist Party members entered shouting various slogans like "Red Front." After three bell rings, Ms. Sittkin, supported by two other female Communist members, ascended to the speaker's seat. Surprisingly, the 230 members of the National Socialist Party, who nearly constituted half of the entire assembly, did not obstruct the proceedings. Even though the speaker's opening remarks contained some provocative language, they remained unmoved, evidently following the orders of their party leader. During the speaker's address, the National Socialist members sat silently, while the National People's Party members left the chamber together, only to return when it came time to vote. The speaker's speech was met with cheers from the Communist members, but was otherwise received coldly. Subsequently, it was decided to elect the executive officers, a move that deviated from German parliamentary practice and was also quite astonishing. Its purpose was evidently to use the speaker to pressure the president, avoiding the dissolution or suspension of the parliament. Subsequently, National Socialist member Göring was elected speaker with 307 votes. Only the Social Democrats and the Communists did not vote for him. This demonstrates that the National Socialists and the Catholic Center Party had reached an agreement on this matter beforehand, but it does not necessarily prove that the two parties had also compromised on forming a new coalition government. The two deputy speakers, Graf from the National People's Party and Rochus from the Bavarian People's Party, were elected with the same majority. Then, the new speaker, Göring, took the stage and delivered a concise and sharp speech, refuting rumors that the parliament would be excluded and not allowed to participate in state affairs. He also requested the entire assembly to authorize him to send a telegram to the president, urging him to receive the parliament officials to hear their report on the political situation. He continued, "I solemnly declare before the entire German nation that today's meeting, especially the election of the executive officers, has fully demonstrated that the new parliament has a harmonious working majority. Therefore, there is no reason to dissolve it due to urgent national issues." After the entire assembly granted the speaker the necessary power to handle this matter, the session was adjourned, with the date of the next meeting to be decided by the speaker.

▲Berlin, Reuters, 30th – The new speaker, Göring, is an army captain and a key figure in the Nazi Party. He commanded an air squadron during the European War. The temporary speaker, Sittkin, is a 75-year-old woman and a Communist Party member known as the "grandmother of the revolution." In her opening remarks, Sittkin demanded the impeachment of President Hindenburg and his cabinet for violating the constitution. Sittkin denounced the current cabinet as tools of capitalists and large landowners. Because of being the oldest member of the parliament, Sittkin was chosen as the temporary speaker to conduct the opening ceremony. The National Socialists had opposed Sittkin's appointment as speaker in the past few weeks, but yesterday Hitler decided that the party members must act in an orderly manner to set an example for the nation, and, especially when the parliament is struggling with von Papen, not give von Papen an excuse to implement the president's order to resolve the parliament. Therefore, Sittkin was able to become the temporary speaker. After the president's address was read, the parliament adjourned until next week, so that members of the Center Party could attend the Catholic Congress. It is widely expected that the parliament will be dissolved, but the dissolution order has not yet been issued.

President Signs Dissolution Order

Authorizes von Papen to Fully Handle the Situation

Temporarily Postpones Meeting with Representatives of the New Parliament

▲Berlin, Havas Agency, 30th – The circumstances of this session of the German parliament are unprecedented in the history of parliaments in any country. When von Papen met with Hindenburg at Neudeck, the president had already signed the order to dissolve the House of Representatives and handed it to von Papen for safekeeping. Once something happens, it can be announced at any time. Thus, before the new parliament had even been successfully organized, it had already been sentenced to death. However, von Papen may not exercise the power of dissolution within a few days because von Papen's cabinet has already obtained Hindenburg's full protection and wants to first prove to the public that the various factions in the new House of Representatives are disorganized, have differing opinions, and cannot work properly before issuing the dissolution order.

▲Berlin, National News Agency, 31st – After being elected speaker, National Socialist member Göring telegraphed President Hindenburg, requesting to present the current situation of the parliament and the steps to organize a normal parliamentary government. After receiving Göring's telegram, Hindenburg replied that he would return to Berlin in a few days and would sincerely receive the representatives of the parliament at that time. Therefore, no major events are expected to occur between the parliament and the government in the next three or four days, because von Papen's statement of government policy to the parliament will have to wait until September 4th or 5th, and before that date, the parliament does not really have much important work to do.

Reiterate Demand for Military Equality

German Defense Minister Publishes an Article

▲Berlin, National News Agency, 30th – Today, German Defense Minister Schleicher published an important article in the "Hermesdorf" magazine, elaborating on the need for Germany's military to be equal to that of the major powers. Schleicher stated that the previous disarmament conferences not only failed to pay attention to Germany's reasonable demands, but also increasingly consolidated the existing system, which Germany can no longer tolerate. Schleicher further stated that if the countries do not have the sincerity to jointly reduce armaments in the future, then the increase in Germany's armaments is inevitable due to the pressure of the situation. Germany's powerful neighbors have already fully armed themselves from head to toe, and their national defense security, according to their own experts, is already completely secure. However, Germany's military is labeled with names such as nationalism and imperialism. In fact, what the German people desire is permanent peace and the peaceful existence and development of the nation. But in the current international situation, it is difficult for the German people to live and work in peace. The countries have built barriers on their borders, while Germany alone is not allowed to take measures to defend itself. Is this fair? Schleicher concluded that Germany does not want to immediately join the international arms race, but hopes to use its own resources to strengthen its national defense.

Japanese Red Movement

Young Students' Ideologies Lean Left

Influence Spreads to Business and Industry

Authorities Severely Suppress, Over a Thousand Reported

▲The Osaka Asahi Shimbun reports that since the repeated investigations of the Communist Party, there has been a resurgence of red reading groups organized by the education sector, the Communist Youth League, attempting to rebuild its activities, and its influence is quite strong. Participants in the group include Osaka High School, Osaka Commercial University, Naniwa High School, Kansai University, Kansai Gakuin, Osaka Dental College, Osaka Foreign Language School, and other schools. The members are all young students who directly promote red ideals and have established the Osaka Youth Communist League local committee. Its leaders are Hashimoto, Tamaki, Konishi, and Shimoji from Kishiwada Textile Bridge. These individuals incite red ideas within their respective schools while also participating in practical struggles outside the schools. Funds are provided by the National Council of Trade Unions to promote left-wing cultural movements, frequently distributing leaflets opposing imperialist war, and gradually spreading to factories in various locations. Furthermore, these left-leaning students are mostly the children of wealthy families, including the sons of viscounts, the sons of university presidents in Tokyo, and the nephews of naval admirals. In Osaka alone, there are as many as 172 student members. Public servants, school teachers, company clerks, shop assistants, and employees of various transportation agencies are also being increasingly expanded and strengthened. Especially since the outbreak of the Manchurian Incident last year, at a time when people's hearts were shaken, they distributed anti-war leaflets in the Osaka barracks and army factories, or inserted unstable slogans, documents, and advertisements into items sent to soldiers on the front lines. They secretly investigated the deployment of troops, the construction of military factories, the location of ammunition depots, the location of gunpowder depots, and the names and addresses of senior military officers from company commanders down to the higher echelons. Consequently, soldiers such as Machioka Yuuo, a private first class in the 8th Regiment, were assimilated by the red ideology. Fortunately, thanks to the efforts of the Osaka Prefecture Special Higher Police, the key figures were gradually arrested, preventing a major incident from occurring. Similar unstable red organizations exist in major cities such as Tokyo, Kyoto, and Kobe. Over the past year, over a thousand people have been reported.

Important News

Jehol Rising Up to Resist Japan

History of the Jehol National Salvation Army

Jehol is a remote special region, which has gradually attracted attention since the recent invasion by the Japanese bandits. Its land is rich, not inferior to the Northeast, and its mineral resources are especially abundant. A brief summary of its situation is as follows:

Population: There has never been an accurate count of the population of Jehol. According to official investigations, there are 584,559 households in the entire region, with 2,166,146 men and 1,329,332 women, totaling 3,495,478 people. However, according to local estimates, the population has been increasing in recent years and is actually higher than this number. Approximately, the population of the entire region is over five million.

Climate: Similar to Hebei, with the seasons lagging by half a month. Mineral Resources: Coal and gold are the most abundant, followed by iron, then copper and tin. Asbestos, gemstones, and crystal are also found. The most notable is the petroleum mineral, with a total of four locations. The one in Jiufotang, 99 li south of Lingyuan County, has been repeatedly identified as very promising after many surveys. Unfortunately, the survey report has not been made public, so the details are unknown. There are also locations in Pingning City County. After the extension of our country's suspension, there are no large oil fields in the country. In this era of oil competition, Jehol is a treasure trove and covetted by the Japanese.

Waterfalls and Hydroelectric Power: There is a large waterfall in the northern mountains of Chifeng County. It has been estimated that if a hydroelectric power plant were built, the electricity could supply the entire region.

Culture: The four counties of Pingquan, Lingyuan, Chaoyang, and Chifeng are the most prosperous. Chifeng is the center of Jehol, with commerce concentrated there, and is considered the richest. Pingquan and Lingyuan are known for their talent and culture. Chaoyang is close to Liaoning and is quite prosperous. The remaining counties are mostly undeveloped.

History of the Jehol National Salvation Army: Jehol has a great hero, Huang Shouzhong, who enjoys local prestige. In 1923, the people suffered from the authorities' forced planting of opium and the heavy collection of opium taxes. Huang Shouzhong took the lead, contacted heroes from all over the region, and organized the local self-government army. The following year, Huang went to Beiping in disguise and met with Mr. Sun Yat-sen. Mr. Sun Yat-sen praised his aspirations and appointed Huang as the Special Military Commissioner for Inner Mongolia. Huang worked even harder upon receiving the order, gathered comrades, and secretly worked under the name of the militia, forming eight cavalry teams (each team roughly equivalent to a cavalry regiment), with both guns and horses equipped. This was the beginning of the Jehol National Salvation Army. When the Northern Expeditionary Army rose and the Northwest Army entered Beiping through an indirect route, Huang led his troops to respond, first raising the Blue Sky White Sun flag. The Northwest Army appointed Huang as the Commander-in-Chief of Jehol and fought with the Feng Army for years, eventually securing the entire territory of Jehol. Later, Yan Xishan of the Jin Army appointed Huang as the Commander-in-Chief of the Jehol Security Force. In 1928, Chiang Kai-shek sent Shang Wuzhai to present Huang with the appointment letter of the Commander of the First Cavalry Army of the National Revolutionary Army, ordering Huang to assist the Jin Army and pacify Jehol and Chahar. However, this incurred the jealousy of a certain general in the Jin Army, who, under the guise of issuing pay, lured Huang to Beiping, detained him at the Garrison Headquarters, and issued an order to encircle and attack his subordinates. His subordinates retreated to the border between Jehol and Chahar, protecting the local area and remaining steadfast. Later, with the strong protection of the local people, Huang was released from prison. Huang returned to Jehol, reorganized his troops, and continued to raise the banner of the self-government army, resisting the Jehol authorities' forced planting of opium and all illegal donations and taxes, protecting the people of one region. As a result, the united ranks became even broader, totaling ten militia units with over 30,000 people. When the September 18th Incident occurred, the leaders of the Jehol self-government army gathered in Longhua to discuss countermeasures. Huang strongly advocated that from now on, the guns should be pointed outwards, that past grievances with the Jehol authorities should be abandoned, and that they should unite to resist Japan. It was proposed to rename the self-government army the National Salvation Army, divided into ten routes, with commanders Geng Jizhou, Zhao Yi, Zhang Beifeng, etc. Over 8,000 troops from three routes entered Liaoning one after another and actively resisted Japan. Their battles have been reported in various newspapers. If the authorities can provide them with supplies and encouragement, they will be an extremely powerful anti-Japanese force between Jehol and Liaoning.

Fierce Battle of Ma Zhanshan in Hailun

Japanese Planes Follow and Drop Bombs

Ma Meets with Representatives of the Investigation Team

Japanese Soldiers Massacre in Haibei Town

Ma's Army Isolated and Helpless, Extremely Worrisome

Hailun Correspondence: Chairman Ma arrived in Hailun from Heihe on May 1st. The next day, he led his troops out of the city to fight. At 6:00 AM on May 3rd, six Japanese planes flew in from the direction of Harbin and dropped over 50 bombs over Hailun. They also strafed the city's residents with machine guns. Dozens of sulfur bombs were dropped at the main intersection and the West Market, immediately starting fires that destroyed over 20 large and small businesses, over 30 brothels, and over 10 homes. About 30 people were killed or injured, with losses estimated at around one million yuan. When the bombs were dropped, Chairman Ma was residing in the Guangxintong Trading Company on East Main Street in Hailun. The 400 or so guards he brought were stationed in businesses and hotels and were not injured. Seeing the fire in the street, Chairman Ma personally risked his life to supervise the people in fighting the fire amidst a rain of bombs, loudly shouting for everyone to come and put out the fire. However, with bombs and machine-gun fire raining down, people were too busy trying to escape to even think about fighting the fire. Witnessing this tragedy, Chairman Ma couldn't help but weep in sorrow, saying, "This is the disaster I brought to Hailun," and so on. As he was grieving, Chairman Ma's guards and those around him urged him to return indoors to avoid danger. Chairman Ma said to them, "Don't be afraid. Life and death are destined." He only returned indoors after the Japanese planes left. The planes circled over Hailun for a total of 40 minutes, having exhausted all the bombs they carried. The 2,000 troops that Chairman Ma brought simultaneously fought the Japanese army south of Hailun City. Due to poor weaponry, they lost their combat capability and retreated into the city. On the morning of the 4th, Chairman Ma led his troops north, retreating 45 li to Haibei Town (also known as Dazhutang), where they stayed overnight. That same day, another Japanese plane came to Hailun to scout and dropped several bombs. On the 5th, Chairman Ma retreated from the Catholic Church toward the border of Tongbei County. The main force headed due north, while Chairman Ma retreated toward the southwest of Haibei Town. An hour before Chairman Ma left the town, another Japanese plane came to scout over the town's streets. It then quickly flew to a point 10 li north of the town, dropped two bombs into the ranks, and returned south. That day, Chairman Ma went to a villager's home in Moshizi Shijing to meet with representatives of the League of Nations investigation team. He reported in detail the war situation of the violent Japanese invasion of the Northeast and the Huhai line. After Chairman Ma parted with the representatives, he personally led 2,000 troops southward. At 3:00 PM on the 6th, two Japanese planes flew in from Harbin and arrived over Haibei Town, dropping over 20 bombs and firing machine guns, killing 19 innocent men and women and injuring four. The planes circled for half an hour before flying away. On the 7th, two more planes came to Zejia Town (in Tongbei County), 40 li north of Haibei Town, dropping bombs and killing and wounding six people. Because the town had only about 30 households, the casualties were not high. On the 9th, two more Japanese planes came to the skies over Tongbei County, dropping bombs and killing or wounding three or four residents. Again, because the county was sparsely populated, with only about 100 households in the entire city, not many people were injured. After bombing the two counties of Hai and Tong and various towns, the Japanese planes went to explode in the Longzhen County Nanbei'an area and also bombed Keshan County, Kedong County, Dedu County, and other places. The number of people injured is unknown but likely not small. In short, the entire Jiang Province, except for the frontier counties far away, suffered from the bombing. All counties within a thousand li of Harbin, Hailun, Suihua, and Bokui were not spared. Therefore, there are Japanese airstrips everywhere. The situation in places already occupied by the Japanese army is especially tragic.

When 500 Japanese soldiers first arrived in Hailun, they stayed in various businesses, not moving into the old military camps of our army. Later, over 2,000 more soldiers were successively added, totaling over 3,000. Various obstacles were set up in the main streets and alleys to prevent our army from attacking. Barbed wire was used to weave obstacle nets in the middle of the alleys, with doors left open during the day and closed at night. At every intersection and main street, sandbag bunkers were built and guarded day and night. Later, 300 Japanese infantry and cavalry also arrived in Haibei Town to garrison it, with the same equipment as in Hailun. When Infantry Major Ishikawa Shigeru entered the town, he engaged in public buying and selling. Unexpectedly, on the night of June 10th, Deng Wen, the brigade commander under Chairman Ma, sent over 200 cavalry from a certain regiment to sneak across the town moat and enter the town, opening fire on the Japanese guards. The two sides immediately started fighting, fighting for about five hours. At dawn, our army withdrew, killing over ten Japanese soldiers, wounding six or seven, and capturing four alive. Our side had five or six soldiers killed in action. Unexpectedly, after our army retreated, the Japanese falsely accused the residents of Haibei Town of colluding with outsiders. They then stabbed and buried alive 108 residents of the town and villagers who came to the market early in the morning. Any able-bodied men they encountered were killed with bayonets and buried on the spot. Regardless of whether it was in the center of the street or in the alleys, graves were everywhere. Captain Ishikawa then reported to Brigade Commander Hiraga Teizo that the residents of Haibei Town were all in league with Ma and that there were no good people. He requested that the entire town be destroyed with artillery fire. On the 12th, the Japanese dispatched an artillery detachment, carrying several mountain guns, from Hailun's north gate toward Haibei Town. While traveling to the Qixingpao area, the artillery vehicles got stuck in a mud ditch and could not be pulled out. Later, through the pleas of the director of the Hailun Collection Bureau and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce to Commander Hiraga, the disaster of destruction was averted. The 8,000 lives of Haibei were almost tragically poisoned. Although this battle turned out to be a blessing in disguise, sporadic abuse was unavoidable. From then on, the Japanese army arbitrarily robbed merchants and civilians for food, lodging, and purchases. They also secretly colluded with Koreans to forcibly rob and extort money. All kinds of situations are difficult to describe in detail. The Japanese in Hailun received many secret letters every day. If someone harbored a grudge and secretly reported someone to the Japanese, falsely accusing them of being Chairman Ma's spy, they would be arrested, immediately shot, and buried alive. In Hailun, the streets were cleared every day at 8:00 PM. Anyone who was even slightly late would be killed without exception. Since May 4th, businesses in Hailun and Haibei have been completely closed. Although they were later forced to reopen, without farmers coming to the market, opening the door was the same as closing it. The disaster in Haibei Town was even worse than in Hailun because Haibei was a necessary route to Tongbei, Keshan, and other places. Japanese troops going north were bound to pass through it. Later, the Japanese again forced people to carry ammunition and supplies. If they tried to escape, they would be shot. All the vehicles, horses, and cattle in the town had fled. In the end, only one-tenth of the residents remained in the town.

The wealthy villagers of the Northeast usually prepared firearms and built walls and bunkers. At this moment, they have all been broken and looted. As far as the counties of Jiang Province are concerned, the people suffered such a tragic disaster at the hands of the Japanese army that it surpassed the time when Korea was destroyed. Currently, in Jiang Province, besides a portion of Chairman Ma's army, there are seven brigades including Cheng, Tu, Su, Pu, Zhou, Jia, and Zhang, who have surrendered to Japan. These troops have recently been chasing after Ma's army, and the two sides have engaged in several fierce battles, killing each other. Currently, Chairman Ma has retreated to the mountainous area east of Tieli County. His subordinates number only about 10,000 people and are in great danger under the pursuit of the Japanese army. Japanese planes follow and bomb them all day long. They move every night and hide in rural villagers' homes during the day. Currently, Deng Wen and Li Haiqing's armies, numbering about 10,000, attacked Haibei Town before July 20th because there were over 100 Japanese soldiers in Haibei surveying the route, planning to extend the Huhai Railway from Hailun northward to Keshan County and connect it with the Tao'ang Railway. Construction will begin soon, and it is scheduled to be completed to Haibei Town by the end of August. This section is 45 Chinese li long. Chairman Ma is eager to destroy this plan.

Most worrying is that Chairman Ma's army has fallen into a state of isolation and extreme danger. If the central government does not send troops soon, it will be difficult to sustain for long. Because the Japanese army is determined to defeat Chairman Ma, they coordinate land and air attacks every time they engage Ma in battle. The air force, in addition to dropping bombs, also serves as artillery targeters. The artillery fire is extremely fierce. Ma's army has no air defense weapons and can only use flesh and blood to resist the enemy. There is no good strategy. Ammunition is especially scarce.

The Tragedy of the Harbin Flood

The Puppet Government Had No Disaster Prevention Preparedness

Japanese Military Police Took the Opportunity to Oppress Disaster Victims

The Entire City Became a Marsh, Few Escaped

Harbin Correspondence: After being ravaged by the Japanese, Harbin had barely extinguished the flames of war when it was tragically flooded on August 7th. Except for the elevated Qinjiagang and Majiagou areas, the entire city was underwater. The water was deepest in Daowai, ranging from eight chi to one zhang, five or six chi, disrupting transportation. Boat traffic was necessary in the city. Telephone and electric lights were also cut off. In Daoli, the area around 36 Peng and Zhengyang River was four or five chi deep. The usually prosperous Central Avenue was five chi deep, and transportation could only be done by boat. Puppet government officials paid no attention, causing all 300,000 residents of the city to suffer. To this day, all businesses have stopped, and there is no end in sight to the flooding. The prosperity of Harbin is almost hopeless. The situation is recorded as follows:

The Situation When Water First Rose in Daowai

▲Rivers Rose Greatly: The weather this summer, starting from June 2nd, was rainy every other day, and sometimes it rained continuously for several days and nights. Until late July, the rain did not stop. Various rivers were scoured by mountain floods and fed by tributaries, causing the water level to rise greatly. The Songhua River is the only main stream of various rivers in northern Manchuria, and it received the most flow. Since June 25th, the water volume has been rising daily. Even the usually shallow shoals in the downstream areas of Mantianxing and Sankuishi were more than one zhang deep. Initially, the cities and towns along the river regarded the rising water as a customary event every year and paid no attention to it. They were also negligent in their defenses. By July 25th, Yilan, with its lower terrain downstream and shallow riverbanks, was the first to be flooded. The riverbank was ten li away from the city, but the water still overflowed and entered the entire city. By the 28th, the entire city was submerged in water. At the same time, the Mudan River also overflowed its banks. The two rivers merged, and the water depth in the city reached one zhang, four or five chi. Even the shallowest areas were over five chi deep. Homes and government buildings were all in the water. Countless people and animals died. Disaster victims struggled in the water, fleeing to nearby mountains and living in the open air. Because food and supplies had been submerged, many victims had nothing to eat and picked leaves to fill their stomachs. Although boats were used in the city, they were requisitioned by the Japanese military and puppet government agencies. Weak families were unable to break free. Countless people were washed away by the flood. However, at this time, Harbin upstream still believed that the flood would not come suddenly, so no precautions were taken.

▲Water Forces Harbin: After July 29th, the Songhua River rose rapidly by one or two chi per day. The embankments of Bin City had only four chi exposed above the water. The embankment was built in August of the ninth year of the Republic of China, starting from First Avenue Street in Binjiang City and ending at Eighteenth Avenue Street in Binjiang City. The entire line was over 430 zhang long. From Eighteenth Avenue Street to Twentieth Avenue Street, it turned to the base of Jiajiagang, a high ground, which was an old-style earthen embankment. The entire line was 280 zhang long. When the river rose greatly in the twelfth year of the Republic of China, the Binjiang gentleman silk organization's River Embankment Project Office added a two-chi-wide and three-chi-high brick dam on top of the stone dam. However, the project was very simple. Since the addition, the water has not exceeded the stone dam, so it is not known whether the brick dam is effective. The river water in the past was mostly about three zhang away from the dam and never reached the base of the dam. After the water rose, the river widened. This time, the water reached the base of the dam and gradually rose higher. The Harbin International Association, seeing that no puppet government officials paid attention, risked violating the strict news censorship and published news that the rising river water threatened people's lives. This lasted for a week. At that time, the water level had risen to within half a chi of the stone dam, leaving only the one or two chi of brick dam added in the twelfth year. At this time, the Binjiang gentry merchants and puppet government officials began to pay attention. However, they all had the mentality of benefiting from their neighbors, thinking that the northern bank of Jiang, Machuankou, and Songpu Town were lower in elevation. If the river rose further, the water would definitely flow to the northern bank, and the southern bank would be safe. Therefore, although the River Embankment Project Office, led by the Chamber of Commerce, held two meetings, they were full of disputes and could not come up with a solution. In the end, they only slightly prepared sandbags and piled them up at the intersections of the docks on Seventh, Twelfth, and Eighteenth Avenue Streets in Binjiang City. Although the merchants and civilians were panicked, they still hoped that the brick dam would not collapse. But at 8:00 AM on the 4th, the river rose again. Machuankou on the northern bank, with its lower riverbank, was submerged. The dike first breached behind the Tangguantun Hulan Sugar Factory and flowed in. In less than two hours, the entire city of Songpu and Machuankou was flooded. The vital Xingquan Avenue was about one zhang deep, and the current was very rapid. Even boats could not easily enter. Over 10,000 residents were caught off guard and unable to escape. They all fled to the roofs. Furniture and belongings could not be retrieved. Fortunately, it was daytime, and no one drowned. In the afternoon, the Harbin Red Swastika Society and the Charity Federation hired over ten large ships to transport disaster victims to Harbin to temporarily reside in Nangang. However, the victims were still told to find their own open-air places to stay. After the entire city of Songpu was flooded, the river flowed toward Hulan County. The Hu-Hai Railway in the section of Songpu and Machuankou was washed away in many places. Crops and homes were all washed away. Dozens of villages were flooded. From Machuankou northward for about 70 li, there was an endless expanse of water. (To be continued)

Local Correspondence

Taicang

▲Moxie Newspaper Closed Down: The Moxie Newspaper in our county has been in operation for many years. It was initially changed to a daily newspaper in August, hoping to develop further. Unexpectedly, on the 19th and 28th, due to the publication of an article about business tax, the county government believed that it contained words that incited the people and resisted national taxes. On the 29th, the newspaper was closed down, and the director, Zhu Tieying, was summoned. The county magistrate, Zhao Enju, personally opened the case and sentenced Zhu to one year of imprisonment and a fine of one hundred yuan in accordance with the publication law.

Suzhou

The High Court Sends Personnel to Escort Hu Lifu: The notorious traitor Hu Lifu, since being arrested by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau and transferred to the capital for military law trial, was approved to be handed over to the judicial authorities for handling. It was then assigned to the jurisdiction of the Jiangsu High Court. The Suzhou High Court Prosecutor's Office received a telegram from the Ministry of Justice yesterday (the 31st), ordering the dispatch of personnel to Beijing to escort him. After receiving the order, Chief Wang immediately appointed Secretary Pang to supervise Judicial Policeman Bu Guisheng and Bailiff Ren Bingguang to go to Beijing by car. They are scheduled to escort him to Suzhou this afternoon (the 1st). After the Prosecutor's Office investigates, it will prepare to send him to the Siqian Street Detention Center for detention.

▲The Prosecutor Appeals the Xu Yabo Case: Xu Yabo, the former district chief of the First District of the Provincial Water Police, was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment by the Songjiang County Court for the crimes of joint robbery and receiving stolen goods. He appealed to the High Court. The Third Criminal Division of the High Court, headed by Judge Song, made a judgment on the 19th of this month, revoking the original judgment and acquitting Xu Yabo. The judgment was delivered the day before yesterday. Yesterday, it was learned that the original prosecutor of the case, Wang Shicheng, declared that he was dissatisfied with Xu's acquittal and filed an appeal. The written appeal was notified to Xu Yabo yesterday (the 31st), ordering him to submit a defense if he had any reasons.

▲Lake Bandits are Active in the Countryside Again: On the morning of the 31st, over 30 bandit boats carrying two to three hundred bandits were discovered on the waters of Baxian River and Taishi Dian River between Zhouzhuang and Chenmu. They were moving southwest. Upon hearing the news, the Second Detachment of the Jiaozhi Police Station urgently telegraphed Zhouzhuang, Chenmu, Chefang, and Guoxiang to be on guard. It also dispatched troops to gather at Chefang to intercept them. On the city side, the Third District of the Water Public Security Bureau also dispatched two warships to join the military and police and set off for Chenghu to meet the bandits. Also, the Water Patrol Second Squad of the Police Team encountered four bandit boats carrying over sixty bandits from Henan on the Zhuangzi Bridge between Dongshan and Hengjing at 6:00 AM on the 30th. They immediately opened fire to suppress them. The bandits also returned fire. After half an hour, the bandits fled to South Taihu. As a result, one kidnapped person was shot down.

Wuxi

▲Various Counties Vigorously Contend for Half of the Acreage Surtax for Road Construction: The Wuxi County Government previously received a joint telegram from the Finance and Construction Departments, ordering it to remit half of the local surtax of five fen per mu for road construction to the departments for use as funds for the construction of national and provincial highways, and instructing the Finance Bureau to report the collected amount and remit it along with the land tax on a ten-day basis. The county party headquarters and various mass organizations believed that provincial and county administrations each had their own systems and that operating expenses should be kept within boundaries and not mixed, so as not to start a trend of disorder. The surtax for road construction in various counties of Jiangsu Province is a special fund for local construction in the county, used for the construction of county roads. It has always been kept in the custody of the county construction bureau. Moreover, when the surtax was initially levied, the Jiangsu Provincial Government had repeatedly and clearly stipulated the purpose of the fund, and it should not be suddenly overturned, lest there be a suspicion of changing orders every morning and evening. They telegraphed the central and provincial departments separately, requesting that the case of remitting half of the acreage surtax for road construction to the province be revoked in order to maintain local undertakings and avoid confusing finances. At the same time, various counties such as Wuxian, Wujin, Jiangyin, Liyang, and Changshu also filed petitions to the central and provincial departments, requesting the revocation of this case. Subsequently, Construction Department Director Dong brought up the 524th provincial government meeting, which resolved that half of the acreage surtax for road construction in each county should be remitted to the province in order to centralize funds, coordinate the development of branch lines throughout the province, and seek to facilitate transportation throughout the province. It was not to be used for other purposes. Now that the case has been confirmed, it should be earnestly implemented and cannot be changed due to misunderstandings in a few localities. Another circular should be issued for compliance.

▲Substandard Yarn Seized and Scheduled for Burning: The Wuxi Committee for Suppressing Enemy Goods seized ten pieces of substandard yarn at Laoyabang. They reported it to the county party headquarters for instructions. Now, they have received an approval order and have decided at a committee meeting to burn the substandard yarn at the open space west of the train station on the 5th of this month. They have also sent letters to various organizations, inviting them to send personnel to observe at that time.

Zhenjiang

▲Provincial Government Requests Commendation for Two Virtuous Women: Dai Wang Sitian, a virtuous woman from Pi County, remained chaste in her youth and continued the legacy of her aunt, Dai Dong Shumin. In the 17th and 21st years of the Republic of China, she donated a total of 110,000 yuan for the operation of schools and public welfare. Acting County Magistrate Sun of the county petitioned the Jiangsu Provincial Government for commendation. Now, the provincial government believes that the two women pledged in their youth to remain chaste until old age, demonstrating the integrity of ice and frost, and expanded the regulations of the school system, destroying their families to start schools, a situation worthy of commendation. They have requested the Ministry of the Interior to petition the Executive Yuan to forward a request to the National Government for the issuance of plaques and medals of honor, and to add laudatory words to commend their virtue and inspire others.

▲Good Autumn Harvest and Falling Rice Prices: Since the beginning of autumn this year, rice prices have been falling due to sluggish sales, which is unprecedented in the rice market. The weather has been particularly hot in recent days, and new grain from various places is about to be harvested. Rice prices have fallen further. The higher prices are only 14 yuan, while the lowest Saigon rice is only over 9 yuan. It is said that those in the industry say that if the weather does not change, the autumn harvest will be abundant, and the price of new rice will continue to fall. This is good news for the future of the people's food.

Yangzhou

▲Bandits Rob Grain Shop and Burn Owner: In Gongjin Township, Sixth District of the county, on the night of the 28th, dozens of bandits armed with Mauser pistols rushed to the home of Yang Tingzhen, the owner of the Lu Chen rice shop, and looted it clean. They burned Yang Tingzhen badly and demanded that Yang hand over silver dollars. After searching for several hours, they fired their guns and dispersed. Yang has crossed the river to the Hongjiang Hospital for treatment. His family has come to the city to report the case. It is also said that the bandits who were previously discovered by Sun Tan Xuewen in the case of the kidnapped six-year-old child, Ye Shihua, lived in the west of Yingxu Lake. Today (the 30th), the county detective team has dispatched detectives Ma Chunshan and Gao Lian to lead a team by boat to Bao to investigate the victims and arrest the bandits.

Nantong

▲Large Group of Kidnappers Not Found: According to confidential reports from military and police agencies, a large group of kidnappers from Hongze Lake, holding many kidnapped men and women, secretly came to Nantong and stayed in various hotels on Taowu Road to negotiate ransoms. They searched various hotels, but the bandits and hostages had left the day before.

Rugao

Local News

Shanghai Probably Will Not See War Again

Talks with Commander Dai

Observations by Ariyoshi

According to the Central News Agency, rumors have been rampant in the city these days, almost all saying that a second war is about to break out in Shanghai. As a result, residents in Zhabei and Nanshi have been relocating continuously for days. The panic is almost the same as before the January 28 Incident. Yesterday, the public was even more alarmed, and more people moved. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically visited Dai Ji, commander of the Songhu Garrison, and Yano, acting Japanese Minister to China, to inquire about the truth of these rumors. Commander Dai and Ariyoshi, Counselor of the Japanese Consulate, provided detailed answers. The details are as follows:

▲Dai Ji's Talk The Central News Agency reporter visited Dai Ji, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, at the headquarters yesterday morning to inquire about the recent installation of military telephones by the Japanese army stationed in Shanghai and various rumors circulating outside. The reporter asked if the headquarters had received any formal reports on these matters. According to Dai, although these rumors are mostly groundless, some points are supported by facts. For example, the headquarters has received formal and concrete reports about the Japanese army installing military telephones in western Shanghai. As for their intentions, outsiders cannot fathom them. Because the Japanese army is well-trained, military secrets are difficult for the outside world to discover. This patriotic movement has achieved considerable results. The Japanese side's preparations may be for this reason. As for the rumors that a second war is about to break out in Shanghai, according to my observation, it may not come to this. In the January 28 Incident, the Japanese side did not gain any advantage. This time, they probably won't sacrifice money and lives again in vain. However, the Japanese side hates our country's patriotic movement and may use it as an excuse to expand the issue. We must take precautions. Therefore, I hope those involved in the patriotic movement will be extra cautious to avoid giving the Japanese side any pretext. As for public security in the urban area, I will do my best to maintain it. In Zhabei, there are security teams maintaining security. In Nanshi, there is a regiment of troops newly arrived from Zhejiang Province and police stationed there. There is no need to worry about maintaining normal public security. There are already more than three thousand Japanese troops in Shanghai, and their firearms are sophisticated. If they disregard everything and act, I, as a soldier, have a responsibility to defend the territory. I will do my best to fulfill my duty. The reporter also asked that recently, the Northeast Volunteer Army's counter-offensive is extremely urgent. Is the Japanese side concentrating the Third Fleet to disturb the Yangtze River area to create a diversion? Dai replied that the three northeastern provinces have been invaded, and they are now planning to use all their strength to seize Rehe. If our country proceeds to recover lost territory, Japan will definitely demonstrate and create a diversion in the Yangtze River area, and so on.

▲Japanese Statement The Central News Agency reporter then visited Yano, Acting Japanese Minister to China, at the Japanese Consulate. Because Yano was out on official business, Ariyoshi, First-Class Chinese Counselor, received the reporter. According to Ariyoshi, the six-point plan for Japan to disturb Shanghai again, as reported in the newspaper this morning, is completely inaccurate. The reporter also asked that recently, the Japanese army stationed in Shanghai has installed military telephones in western Shanghai and conducted armed demonstrations, causing panic among all sectors, who believe that a second war is about to break out. What does the Japanese side have to say to alleviate the public's panic? Ariyoshi replied that he is not very clear about the situation in Shanghai. However, according to his observation, Shanghai probably will not see a second war again.

Japanese Consulate Explains Rumors

According to the New Sound News Agency, rumors have been spreading for days that Japanese plainclothes soldiers and Red Shirt gangs are appearing in Zhabei and other places from time to time, causing residents there to relocate one after another. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency specifically inquired about these two matters with Japanese Consul Shirai Yasushi yesterday, requesting an explanation. According to Shirai, there are no Japanese plainclothes soldiers appearing in Zhabei. The origin of these rumors is mostly due to ignorant people seeing Japanese people traveling to and from Zhabei, suspecting them of being plainclothes soldiers, and spreading the rumor from one person to ten, and from ten to a hundred, causing the rumors to spread throughout Shanghai. In fact, most of these Japanese people traveling to and from Zhabei are Japanese residents living in Zhabei, and their range is only near North Sichuan Road. Those further away cannot see them. As for the so-called Red Shirt Gang, the municipal government has not protested to the Japanese consulate. However, if such organizations disturb the security of the concession, the Japanese authorities will definitely take action to suppress them.

Yesterday, a Japanese-language newspaper in this city reported that Japanese Navy Commander Sugisaka will demand that Chinese newspapers cancel articles containing [anti-Japanese] and [insulting to Japan] content, and stated that he is determined to take decisive measures. The method will probably be the same as the treatment of the "Min Guo Daily" before the Shanghai Incident. The situation seems quite dangerous. However, the Japanese consul said that Sugisaka only told Japanese reporters that he will demand that Chinese newspapers suppress news containing [anti-Japanese] and [insulting to Japan] content, and there is no such thing as imitating the handling of the "Min Guo Daily."

Residents of Zhabei and Hongkou Moved South Again Yesterday

The Intersection of the Chinese and Concession Areas Was Blocked

The Public Security Bureau Sent Police to劝阻 (persuade and stop) Without Success

According to the Guowen News Agency, due to various rumors in Zhabei and Hongkou recently, generally nervous people are relocating again. Starting at dawn yesterday, people carrying luggage and hiring cars moved south to take refuge in the concession. The intersection of the Chinese and concession areas, such as Baoshan Road, Kaifeng Road, and Qiujiang Road, was blocked for a time. The Fourth and Fifth District Offices of the Municipal Public Security Bureau separately sent police to persuade and stop them, but it was ineffective.

Telegraph Bureau Workers Striked for Two Hours Yesterday

The Request for a Pay Raise Was Not Fulfilled, So They Went on Strike

The Business Director Mediated and Resumed Work

Because the telegraph workers' request to improve treatment and increase wages was not fulfilled, a half-day strike occurred on August 2. Subsequently, Zhong Xun, Director of the Telegraph Administration, accepted the request and set a pay raise of two yuan per person, which was implemented in stages, and then work was resumed. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. However, yesterday, the telegraph workers in this city suddenly announced a strike again at 3:00 p.m. The reporters immediately rushed to investigate and learned that it was still due to the pay raise issue. According to the workers, when they requested a pay raise in early August, Director Zhong promised that the telegraph bureau workers and the radio station workers would implement it at the same time starting in August. When the radio station workers were paid on August 25, the approved pay raise of two yuan was paid out. However, the official order for the telegraph bureau workers' pay raise has not yet been approved. On the 26th, representatives were sent to meet with the director to inquire about the matter. The director sent Li Gongwei, director of the cashier section, to meet with them on his behalf. Li promised to forward the representatives' opinions to the director and telegraphed the ministry to request expedited approval. The representatives then withdrew. Yesterday was the day for the bureau workers to receive their monthly salary. When the workers received their salary, they saw that the approved pay raise of two yuan had not been added. They again sent representatives to question the director. The bureau replied that they had not received an approval order. The representatives immediately reported back to the workers. As a result, the 55 workers were very dissatisfied and decided to go on strike to urge the authorities to realize the situation. Fei Hengfu, the bureau's business director, believed that the workers' strike was of great importance to transportation. He took the initiative to mediate with the workers' representatives. After several consultations between the bureau and the workers, the result was that before the approval order for the pay raise was received, the two yuan of wages that each worker should receive would be temporarily advanced by the bureau starting from that day. The workers were satisfied and resumed work at 5:00 p.m., delivering telegrams as usual.

The Sanyou Factory Dispute Was Arbitrated at the Municipal Government Yesterday

The Employer Did Not Send a Representative to Attend

The Result Was Officially Announced

According to the Dagong News Agency, the long-delayed Sanyou Industrial Society factory closure dispute was formally submitted to arbitration at the Municipal Government Auditorium at 3:00 p.m. yesterday. All the arbitration committee members and labor representatives were present, but the employer was absent at the last minute. The result has been announced. The details are recorded as follows:

▲The Arbitration Process The arbitration officially began at 3:00 p.m. yesterday. Those present were Luo Panhui (Municipal Government), Chairman of the Arbitration Committee, Lu Jingshi (Municipal Party Headquarters), Yang Peng (Special District First Court), Pang Shurong (Local Court), Xu Jilong (Municipal Chamber of Commerce), Zhao Shusheng (General Labor Union), Gong Yuting and Xia Zhongzhao, labor representatives, and Chen Tian, ​​recorder. Zhou Xuexiang and Shao Xubai from the General Labor Union also attended. The employer only submitted a petition and did not send a representative to attend. First, Counselor Luo Panhui, Chairman, declared that the Sanyou Factory dispute had been delayed for a long time. The Social Affairs Bureau was repeatedly ordered to organize a mediation committee to implement mediation, but it was ineffective. Now, the municipal government has received a telegram from the central government and requests from both parties, so it is specifically submitting it to arbitration. Although the employer is not present today, there is no problem. Therefore, it is still officially arbitrating according to the law. Then, the labor representatives stated the process of the dispute, hoping that the members would make a final and fair ruling to relieve the workers' suffering. Then, the arbitration committee members raised questions about the two fires in the factory and whether there were any difficulties in starting the factory, which were answered in detail by Gong Yuting, the labor representative. The meeting was then adjourned.

▲Announcement of the Ruling After the arbitration was adjourned, the arbitration committee members went to the conference room on the second floor to hold an arbitration meeting. They immediately decided on four measures. Each member signed the main text of the draft and announced the official ruling. The full text of the ruling will be officially released after the reasons are supplemented. The content principles are as follows: (1) Restore the work of the Shanghai factory, at least one-fifth of the total. If it cannot be restored immediately, a preparation period of three months is allowed. During the preparation period, food should be provided to the workers according to the original maintenance fee amount. (3) The remaining employees should be dismissed in accordance with the original labor-capital contract. (4) If the Shanghai and Hangzhou factories need to add workers, they should give priority to hiring from the dismissed workers.

▲Pan Xulun's Statement Accountant Pan Xulun sent a letter to Sanyou Industrial Co., Ltd. yesterday, making a statement regarding the factory closure audit. The draft letter is as follows: [To Whom It May Concern: I have checked the advertisements published by your company in the local newspapers, which stated that our company had to close the factory due to irresistible war damage, and the Social Affairs Bureau ordered accountant Pan Xulun to review and verify the evidence. This accountant was ordered to review your company's accounts and only reported all facts in accordance with the points inquired by the Social Affairs Bureau. As for whether your company's factory closure was necessary, it should be decided by the competent authority with reference to the facts. This accountant's audit report does not contain any such proof. Your company's advertisement is deeply afraid of causing misunderstandings among all parties. I hereby make a statement and ask you to check and correct it. Sincerely, Sanyou Industrial Co., Ltd.]

Xu Chongdao's Labor Dispute Was Mediated by the Party and Government Yesterday Without Success

The Labor Side Proposed Four Demands

The Employer Filed a Petition Asking the Authorities to Strictly Stop It

More than 200 employees of all branches of Xu Chongdao Chinese Medicine Store in the city suddenly launched a joint strike the day before yesterday. Party and government agencies, together with representatives of the pharmaceutical industry trade union, rushed to mediate yesterday, but the mediation failed due to the labor and management sides holding different views.

▲Party and Government Mediation After this incident occurred, in order to quickly resolve it, the party and government agencies dispatched Yu Zhongbiao of the People's Training Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters and Zhu Guilin of the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, together with Fang Qingjian, director of the Pharmaceutical Industry Trade Union, Wang Youling and Sun Zixue, representatives of the Xu Chongdao group, and Zhang Mei'an, representative of the industry association, to mediate at the main store on Avenue Edward VII at 4:00 p.m. yesterday. The mediation failed due to the two sides holding different views.

▲Four Demands According to the labor spokesperson, after Zheng Peiran was detained and released, all employees heard the news and immediately convened a team leader meeting. Seven representatives were elected to negotiate with the employer, but they were rejected. A general meeting of all members was reconvened and it was decided to strike to assist them. A strike committee of 23 people, a maintenance team of 21 people, and a transportation team of 5 people were elected to be responsible for carrying out all matters, and four conditions were agreed upon: (1) Dismiss Qu Min and Lou Hechao, the manager of the Seventh Branch. (2) Compensate Zheng Peiran for the loss of reputation. (3) Guarantee the safety of all employees in the future. (4) Pay wages as usual during the strike period and bear all losses by the employer. We will never resume work until the goal is achieved.

▲Store Petition Presented in order to accuse and coerce, illegally strike, endanger business and people's livelihood, please give a strict ruling according to law, and order the resumption of work. The subordinate branch No. 7 is located in the Zhongzhong Road. At about 5:00 a.m. on August 28, when Zheng Peiran, an employee of our store, returned to the store from outside, he noticed that valuable Chinese goods such as ginseng, swallow's nest, and deer antler were missing from the display cabinet. The number was very large, estimated to be worth about 400 yuan. The branch manager Lou Heming telegraphed our general manager and asked for instructions. Our general manager believed that the theft case was criminal, so he telegraphed Qu Ming, the branch manager of the No. 1 branch, to issue a loss sheet and report it to the relevant police station. Later, a detective from the police station came to the store to investigate and believed that the case was internal, so he interrogated all the employees of the branch one by one. As a result, Zheng Peiran looked flustered and his words were contradictory, so he was identified as the most suspected and taken to the police station for questioning. Later, because there was no evidence, Zheng was released and returned to the store. Zheng Peiran falsely accused Qu Ming of deliberately framing him and immediately convened a meeting of all the team leaders of this general branch to request assistance. The team leaders were deceived and decided to request our general manager to immediately dismiss Qu Ming from his position in order to quell public anger. It was found that Qu Ming's report of the theft case to the police station was commissioned by our general manager and did not falsely accuse Zheng Peiran of being the thief. How could it be said that he was framing him? The team leader meeting only relied on Zheng Peiran's false accusation and requested the store to dismiss Qu Ming from his position. Our general manager naturally found it difficult to accept. Unexpectedly, the team leaders convened a general meeting of more than 200 employees from all the branches of this general branch yesterday morning and decided to strike unanimously, only to achieve the purpose of immediately dismissing Qu Ming from his position. This kind of excessive action is disregarding the law. In order to seek an emergency solution and prevent a strike tide, the subordinate branch specifically approved the dispatch of representatives Cen Zhiliang and others to respectfully visit your meeting and ask for prompt relief. The comrade Yu Zhongbiao, sent by your meeting, and the representative Chen Liangping from the Social Affairs Bureau, rushed to the subordinate branch to thoroughly investigate the truth. At that time, Zhao Zhenhui and Fang Qingjian, representatives of the Pharmaceutical Industry Trade Union, and Zhang Mei'an, representative of the Chinese Medicine Industry Association, were all in the subordinate branch to mediate. They also invited various representatives such as Cen Yongkang and Yang Xihui, the chairmen of the small group of the subordinate branch. They all believed that the dispute between Qu Ming and Zheng Peiran was a judicial issue and should be resolved by the judicial authorities and did not involve the store. They also believed that the employees' announcement of the strike without legal procedures was inappropriate and advised them to resume work by a certain date. However, despite the representatives' bitter persuasion, the employees still insisted as before, resulting in no result. Thinking that the pharmaceutical industry is related to people's livelihood and that the strike violates the prohibited regulations, the employees are only using a strike to coerce the employer because of personal disputes, causing the subordinate branch's business to suffer losses and endangering people's livelihood. I am deeply afraid that if this trend continues, the future of commerce will be unimaginable. I am hereby expressing my distress and respectfully ask your meeting to strictly rule according to the law and order all the employees of the subordinate branch to resume work by a certain date in order to respect the law. Otherwise, in order to defend itself, the subordinate branch will take decisive measures. I am at a loss for words to express my urgent desire to obey the order.

▲Corrected News The employer of the store believed that there were discrepancies with the facts in the news published by the Dagong News Agency yesterday, so they specifically sent a letter to correct it. The news about the labor unrest in our store published in your newspaper yesterday stated that the police detectives identified Zheng Peiran as a suspect of theft and immediately arrested him. The employees were shocked and specifically requested the general manager Cen Zhiliang to bail Zheng Jun from the police station within one hour. This is inconsistent with the facts. Zheng Peiran was taken to the police station for questioning by the detectives because of contradictory words and was immediately released. There was no detention, and the employees did not request the general manager to bail Zheng Jun. I am sincerely afraid that this will cause misunderstandings from the outside world. Please correct it in your newspaper to clarify the facts.

▲Business as Usual The store has been operating as usual for two days since all the employees suddenly went on strike on a pretext. Because the pharmaceutical industry strike is related to people's livelihood and is very important, in order to supply the needs of patients and maintain social stability, during the strike period, they have exhausted all efforts to distribute all the dozens of senior employees of the store to all the branches to take charge of various departments such as retail, wholesale, prescription medicine, and medicine preparation for customers.
