The Shanghai Nanshi Public Bus Company Paid Off Back Wages Yesterday After Closing

The Request for Dissolution Fees Will Be Mediated at a Later Date

After the Shanghai Nanshi Public Bus Company's board of directors decided to temporarily suspend operations, all the workers put forward conditions. The day before yesterday, the party and government agencies mediated the labor-capital dispute, which temporarily came to an end. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Decided Measures The Social Affairs Bureau dispatched Peng Zhenqiu and the Municipal Party Headquarters dispatched Fan Guoren to rush to the company at 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday to thoroughly investigate the truth and mediate accordingly. The workers put forward the following conditions: (1) Pay off the back wages. (2) A dissolution fee of six months' wages per worker. (3) Give priority to hiring old workers when resuming operations. The representatives of the party and government agencies, together with the workers' representatives Hu Jinshan, Zhou Anshan, Qiao Jihe, Gu Yongquan, Gu Alin, Qian Shunmao, Yin Changlin, Wu Junhui, Tao Baoyu, etc., and the company manager Shen Hegao and liquidator accountant Jiang Wanping, negotiated a solution. It was decided that (1) the wages for the second half of August and the 70% of the wages owed in March would be paid on August 31. (2) The dissolution fee, etc., will be mediated by the party and government agencies in accordance with the law.

▲Yesterday's Back Wages Were Paid Yesterday, all the public buses on all routes in Shanghai Nanshi were still completely suspended. All the workers gathered at the intersection of Xiexu Road and Jumen Road. The order in the factory was maintained by the Public Security Bureau police. Fan Guoren from the Party Headquarters went to the factory to monitor the company's payment of back wages to all the workers. It was not completed until 5:00 p.m. At the same time, the representatives of the party and government agencies advised the workers to return after receiving their back wages. The Social Affairs Bureau decided to formally mediate the dissolution fee, etc., in the shortest possible time and ordered them to elect responsible representatives to wait for the summons. As a result, the workers were satisfied and dispersed.

The Social Affairs Bureau Decided on Two Principles for the Anglo-American Tobacco Factory Labor Unrest

The Result of Summoning Labor and Management for Questioning Yesterday

The Employer Promised to Consider and Respond Tomorrow

All the workers of the Anglo-American Tobacco Factory opposed the factory's management rules, causing a serious labor unrest. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau specifically summoned both labor and management for questioning at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. Li Deque and Cao Yunxiang, representatives of the Anglo-American Tobacco Factory, Gu Ruofeng and Chen Peide, representatives of the Fifth District Cigarette Industry Trade Union, Chairman Wang Gang, and Recorder Wang Zhongqin, first reported on the labor side's submission regarding this case, requesting (1) that the factory implement the Factory Law, (2) that the various established measures of the labor-capital contract be revised, and (3) that the management rules established by the factory be revised. The employer stated that if there are any inappropriate points, they can be revised first through proper procedures. The labor side stated that the rules established by the factory conflict with the Factory Law and the labor-capital contract, and the factory's facts are still in conflict with the management rules themselves. The employer also said that if the facts of the conflict are pointed out, the factory can correct them. As for the factory rules, if they are inappropriate in themselves, they can also be revised. After a long period of debate between labor and management, the chairman finally decided on two principles: (1) The trade union and the factory should both abide by the current labor laws and regulations. (2) The factory's usual methods of treating workers should still be followed if they are superior to the current laws and regulations. All relations between labor and management should be examined based on the above two principles. If there are any violations, they will be revised. The labor side was satisfied, and the employer promised to consider and respond at 9:00 a.m. on Friday.

The Labor Unrest of the Chafang of the Datong Vessels

Due to Filling Out Application Forms and Searching for Guarantees Again

The Middle Cabin Guild Petitioned Yesterday

The Chafang of the Datong Renji Shipping Company's Zhida, Longda, Zhengda, and Hongda vessels launched a labor unrest due to opposing the company's forcing them to fill out application forms. The Middle Cabin Guild petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Cause of the Labor Unrest The Datong Company announced that all the Chafang of each vessel must fill out application forms and search for guarantees again. All the workers believed that according to the usual practice of sailors across the country, there is no need to fill out application forms. The Datong Company's announcement this time clearly violates past practices. Moreover, the so-called compliance with the company's new regulations in the application form has not been approved by the government in advance, and it has not been announced to the workers. They unanimously refused to express it. As for the guarantees that have already been deposited in the company, there is no reason to search for them again. They requested assistance from the Shanghai Branch of the Seamen's Association and the Seamen's Middle Cabin Guild. The Shanghai Branch took on the task of mediation to no avail.

▲Workers Petitioned The Seamen's Middle Cabin Guild yesterday sent representatives Zhou Xiaoting, Jiao Langcai, Gao Yongliu, Qian Ziyun, and Zhang Heyun to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition, requesting that the company be stopped from forcing workers to fill out application forms. Zhu Guilin, mediator of the Third Section, received them. Regarding the workers' request, he promised to accept it and convey it to the section chief. It was decided to send personnel to cooperate with the Municipal Party Headquarters to find a solution before September 2. The representatives were satisfied and returned. It is heard that the bureau has scheduled personnel to cooperate with the Municipal Party Headquarters to conduct a thorough investigation this afternoon in order to verify and handle the matter.

Ye Gongchuo Talks About Responsible Transportation

The Road and Business Sides Should Discuss Openly and Frankly

The Railway Should Be Fully Prepared

The Ministry of Railways has promulgated the General Rules for Responsible Transportation of Railways, which will be implemented starting today. Yu Zha, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, came to Shanghai the other day to host people from all walks of life and report on the significance of responsible transportation. The business community has been discussing it frequently in recent days. The reporter believes that this matter is of great importance, so he visited Ye Gongchuo, a senior figure in the transportation industry, to ask for his opinion on responsible transportation. Ye published his views as follows: Ye said that responsible transportation by railways is a common practice in the world. Due to various reasons, some of our country's roads have already implemented it, while others have not. However, in terms of the current world trend, all roads across the country should be handled uniformly. However, before implementation, considerable preparation should be made so that customers do not feel inconvenienced and misunderstandings are not caused. It seems that many road employees are concerned about implementing responsible transportation. But in the case of the Beining and Jiaoji roads, the handling of responsible transportation has not been found to have any adverse results. At the beginning of the Beining Road's implementation, the road employees were very worried about compensating for losses, fearing that the number would be too large and the railway would not be able to bear it. But as a result, the average compensation in a year was only more than 10,000 yuan. In my opinion, no matter what kind of business, it is inevitable that there will be small conflicts of interest at the beginning of the implementation. For the sake of the future of the business, any party should put aside interests and assist in its progress. When the General Rules for Responsible Transportation of Railways promulgated by the Ministry of Railways this time, or when a certain road has special circumstances, special regulations can be made in the implementation rules to make it suitable for the situation of each road in order to facilitate progress. Ordinary merchants often suffer from the complexity of the laws and regulations promulgated by the government, so they lack research, and many benefits are obtained by third parties. In my opinion, it is best for merchants to directly discuss with the railway each other openly and frankly. For points that are considered obstacles, it may be discussed and studied to remove these obstacles. At the same time, the railway should also step up and fully prepare the things that must be prepared, such as vehicles, warehouses, docks, etc. Although the railway finances are currently difficult to the extreme, the railway's subsidy for the circulation of goods must not be neglected. Responsible transportation is a very legitimate business. If you want to do it well and want to have satisfactory results, road employees should also make great efforts. If it is said that the business community opposes it, in my opinion, it may be a temporary misunderstanding. Responsible transportation is a very common thing, and other roads have considerable experience, and there is no obstacle to speak of.

Important News Regarding Responsible Transportation

Telegram from the Railway Department Explaining to the Chamber of Commerce

Various Industries Plan Water Transportation Methods

▲Railway Department Responds to Chamber of Commerce via Telegram The Railway Department responded via telegram yesterday to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's request to revise the articles on responsible transportation, explaining: "To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, your telegram has been received and understood. We have examined the issue of responsible transportation, which is a sound strategy for organizing railway transport and benefiting merchants. It was previously announced by the Ministry of Communications in the tenth year of the Republic of China, with a 10% surcharge on freight rates on record. The current implementation by the Tianjin-Pukou and Shanghai-Nanjing railways requires substantial funding, such as for adding equipment, increasing staff, and compensating for cargo losses. The costs are considerable, and since railway costs have already increased, the 10% surcharge for responsible transport is, in reality, too low to cover costs. The Chamber's submissions are presumably based on misunderstandings. As for the method of charging priority and top-priority freight fees, it is purely for the convenience of merchants. The railway service is entirely for the community, aiming for fast transportation and eliminating the long-standing problem of private sales of railcars. The method is extremely sound. If merchants do not require urgent transportation, the original price still applies, and there is no issue. The railways are not forcing anyone. The Ministry's reception for representatives from all sectors at the Shanghai Banking Association on the 28th was for informational purposes, not to convene a meeting. The request for item-by-item discussion is unnecessary. If businesses have other questions, they can submit them in writing to the Ministry for review. Please comply accordingly." Railway Minister Gu Mengyu.

▲Planning Water Transportation According to a leader in the transportation industry who spoke to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, since the January 28th Incident, railway transportation has been disrupted for a long time, and the interior is also affected by the war, causing extreme economic hardship. Therefore, as soon as the war stopped, goods were shipped to Shanghai for sale. At that time, railway transport was not available, so all goods were transported by ship. After unloading, ships immediately sought cargo to carry back, and the prices were very low, only two-thirds of the railway freight rates. As a result, railway freight has not yet recovered to its former state. Now, the Railway Department wants to increase freight revenue, but instead of reducing freight rates to attract business, it is using responsible transport to promote the development of water transport. This is a mistake. Transportation companies are purely intermediaries and are not greatly affected by changes in freight rates. However, various industries are finding railway transport too expensive and are switching to water transport. The livelihoods of transportation companies are at stake, so they have to engage in water transport to survive. Therefore, a joint meeting of the North and South City Public Associations was held today to discuss concrete measures, and it was decided to work jointly with various stations along the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou railways. As for the comparison of water transport and rail transport in terms of time, except for the Zhenjiang-Nanjing section of the Shanghai-Nanjing line, where water transport takes one day longer, the difference is very small. If merchants still wish to have their goods transported by rail, transportation companies will load them without exception, and will not use water transport to resist the railways.

▲Letter Questioning the Director of Business Affairs Yu Chengzhi, the Director of Business Affairs of the Railway Department, mentioned the large profits of transportation companies and their impact on current freight rates during a reception for various sectors in Shanghai to explain responsible transportation. The Shanghai Transportation Trade Association sent a letter of inquiry yesterday to clarify the truth. The original letter reads: "Regarding Article 4, Items 1, 2, and 3 of the explanatory statement made by our Director at the reception for various sectors to explain responsible transportation: 'On the Beijing-Suiyuan Railway, the railway freight for one car of 20 tons of goods from Tianjin to Beiping is 140 yuan. If handled by a transportation company, they charge 200 yuan. On the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, the railway freight for 40 tons of fourth-class goods from Nanjing to Shanghai is 90 yuan 55 fen. If handled by a transportation company, they charge 132 yuan 72 fen. The railway freight for 21 tons of flour from the Nanjing wharf to Machen Road in Shanghai is 46 yuan 37 fen. If handled by a transportation company, they charge 92 yuan,' and he claimed that this was the truth obtained from investigations, reciting it repeatedly. We are extremely shocked. Although it is true that industry representatives incur costs for reporting, transporting, loading, and unloading on behalf of customers, and should be compensated, the fact that they charge so much more than the railway's freight rates is unheard of unless there are special circumstances. If this is true, not only should our Director condemn it, but these individuals are also the moths of the industry, deeply hated by all members of the industry and should be punished to serve as a warning. Since the Beijing-Suiyuan Railway is outside the scope of our association, and we cannot reach it, we will not inquire about it. However, the second and third items, which occurred on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, greatly damage the reputation and credibility of all members of our association. Moreover, there is also legal responsibility to be borne. The truth must be thoroughly investigated. Since our Director claims that it is the truth obtained from investigations, he must have absolute evidence. We dare to ask that he quickly provide two copies of this evidence, transcribed in full, and send them to us by a specific date so that we can investigate the matter and take appropriate action, and to demonstrate our Director's impartial and responsible sincerity. We are extremely eager to receive clarification."

A Hand Grenade Exploded at the Sino-American Watch Company Last Night

Glass Windows Were Destroyed

Fortunately, No One Was Injured

The Sino-American Watch and Optical Company at 389 Nanjing Road has been in business for many years and has a good reputation in the industry. The company's manager, Dong Zixing, is also an executive committee member of the industry association. Last night, it was reported that the store was bombed, but the thrower was not caught. According to eyewitnesses, around 8:00 PM, as the store employees were taking the clocks and watches displayed in the shop and glass cabinets on both sides to the warehouse, other stores had not yet closed, so the road was very busy. There were many cars traveling on the road. Suddenly, a black object was thrown from a car heading west toward the company. The car did not stop and drove straight west. At the time, the employees were gathered around a round table behind the middle glass cabinet, so they did not notice the object flying in from behind. They only became aware when they heard a loud explosion, and shards of metal flew everywhere, filling the room with sulfur gas. At the same time, the glass windows on the left, right, and middle cabinets were completely destroyed. However, the object thrown was a hand grenade, and the explosive power was relatively weak, so no one was injured. Only one customer was slightly injured on the heel and immediately went to the hospital. The explosion was very loud, and the Zhabei Police Station rushed to the scene upon hearing the news. After questioning the manager, they collected all the remaining metal fragments and kept them for the record. The company's losses were minor.

Summary of Volume IV of the Feetham Report

Volume IV of Judge Feetham's report has now been printed in English by the Public Works Department. The content of this volume is almost entirely devoted to a discussion of the internal administrative procedures of the Public Works Department. The research covers the improvement of the committee system, the powers of the Finance Committee, the appointment and powers of auditors, the term of office and qualifications of directors, and the protection of the status of employees in the bureau, etc. A summary of the contents of this volume is given below:

▲Committee System Should Be Improved Judge Feetham believes that if the number of directors is increased to more than 22 or even 30 in the future, the way the board of directors handles affairs must be changed. Even now, before the number of directors is increased, there are still areas that can be reformed. The current way of conducting business does not emphasize formal procedures, and the benefits of the committee system have not been fully realized. At present, committees conduct preliminary considerations of matters and record their conclusions and recommendations, which are then sent to the board of directors. Committees themselves have no administrative power, so everything must be decided by the board of directors, and the benefits of decentralization have not been seen. However, many of the current committee members are not directors but are hired by the bureau because of their knowledge, experience, or relationships. Since committee members are not all directors, they are restricted by the Land Regulations, and the committee cannot have executive power and can only be in an advisory position.

▲Administrative Officers Have Slightly More Power Since committees do not have administrative power, the current affairs of the board of directors are not particularly important. Generally, the chief officers of the various administrative departments, as well as the Director-General and the Chief Financial Officer, are customarily responsible for handling all routine matters without having to consult the board of directors on everything. However, matters related to administrative policy must await the guidance of the board of directors. However, the distinction between what is routine and what relates to policy is mostly determined by the chief administrative officers themselves. Therefore, the power of the committees is rather limited, while the power of the administrative officers is relatively great. However, the power of the administrative officers is still limited by the following two factors: first, the Director-General has general jurisdiction, and the Chief Financial Officer also has financial supervisory power; second, according to custom and precedent, the Chairman of the Board also has the power to personally supervise. In recent times, the Chairman of the Board has spent a large amount of time in the bureau every day, and the Chairman is often re-elected, so the Chairman has become the link between the administrative officers and the board of directors, and his position has become more important. However, despite the above-mentioned restrictions, there is still the danger that the actions of the administrative officers will occasionally be inconsistent with the views and policies of the board of directors, and that committee members will become alienated from the matter. In the current system, the influence of individual personalities is too great. The committee system should be developed as a safeguard for administration. This does not mean depriving administrative officers of their freedom of action, but the board of directors is responsible to the voters, so the board of directors must be able to supervise the administration of each department well. Regarding the number of committees, Judge Feetham proposes establishing five or six standing committees (the Library and Music Committee would be changed to a special committee) to replace the current eight committees. Their powers should be clearly defined in writing and divided into executive and advisory categories. Regular meetings should be held once every two weeks to reduce the need for circulars. The minutes of the committees should be prepared as separate reports to be submitted to the board of directors for processing and should be made public. As for the number of hired committee members, it should be fixed and not exceed one-third of the total number.

▲Auditors Should Be Clearly Defined The Public Concession Land Regulations stipulate that audits should be conducted and reported to the annual meeting, but there are no regulations on how auditors should be selected, their remuneration, protection, qualifications, and powers. Judge Feetham's recommendations are: (1) The audit should be clearly stipulated as a regular practice; (2) Auditors must be legally qualified persons, and directors and employees of the bureau should not be appointed; (3) If Chinese and foreign taxpayers hold separate meetings in the future, each meeting should elect an auditor; (4) The qualifications of candidates for auditor should be reviewed in advance, and their salaries should be determined by the bureau; (5) Auditors should serve for at least three years; (6) Auditors must have sufficient power to perform their duties; (7) The Transvaal system should be used as a reference to specify the format of the auditor's certificate.

▲Qualifications and Restrictions of Directors According to the Public Concession Land Regulations, only a property qualification is required to serve as a director. However, according to municipal common practice in various places, there are restrictions on who may not serve as a director. The current practice in the Public Concession is that employees of the bureau cannot be elected, because bureau employees are exempt from paying taxes and therefore have no right to vote. If the number of directors is increased in the future and the term of office is extended to two years, the qualifications should be further defined in writing. In addition, if a director is frequently absent or unable to attend meetings for a long time due to various reasons, they should be asked to resign. Also, if the matter under discussion is related to the director's personal financial interests, they should be asked to recuse themselves. There are currently no clear written rules, and it is inconvenient to consider whether or not they should recuse themselves on a case-by-case basis. However, this system of recusal should not be too strict, otherwise, honest businessmen may regard the position of director as a daunting task and be reluctant to take on the responsibility. The only way to remedy this is to make the bureau's contracts with businesses public, which can prevent abuses.

▲Powers of the Finance Committee Should Be Increased Judge Feetham believes that the powers of the Finance Committee should be formally defined so that all important financial measures are discussed by the committee before a report is prepared and submitted to the board of directors. If the system of taxpayer annual meetings is changed in the future, the budget may be finally decided by the board of directors. The Finance Committee must have the power to review the estimated expenditures approved by other committees, the total amount of expenditures, the types of taxes to be levied, and how the revenue should be allocated to various projects. After the budget is approved, the Finance Committee should still supervise each department to prevent overspending and misuse. Under the current system, the power to supervise the use of funds lies with the Chief Financial Officer, but in municipal governments throughout the United Kingdom, the Finance Committee plays a very important role in financial supervision and prior planning. The current Finance Committee rarely meets except to discuss the budget. It should be made to meet regularly throughout the year, and the relationship between the Chief Financial Officer and the committee should be made closer.

▲Permanent Employees Should Be Further Protected Under the current system, bureau employees cannot obtain pensions by law, because employees are limited to three-year contracts, and the bureau has the power to dismiss employees with six months' notice, so employees may not be able to obtain pensions based on their years of service. The Land Regulations should be amended to promote this system, so that employees' service can be permanently guaranteed. As employees of public institutions, it is difficult to ensure that they will not offend public opinion or conflict with the interests of powerful private individuals when performing their duties. It is necessary to ensure their own positions so that they can be unyielding and abide by the law. This is not to protect the individual employees, but to protect the interests of the public. If there is a fundamental change in the administration of the Concession in the future, for the sake of administrative efficiency and the interests of employees, all retirees should be treated fairly, and a large number of experienced employees should be retained to continue all administration. In the current transition period, not only should Chinese be brought in to hold senior positions, but also sufficient qualified foreign employees should be retained and recruited. First, it should be stipulated that employees above a certain grade should be given permanent service after a certain period of probation. Second, an arbitration procedure should be established to judge disputes between the Public Security Bureau and employees. A recruitment committee should be established to recruit employees. All final decisions on issues related to the service of permanent employees, as well as the dismissal of certain employees, should be made by the committee. The committee can also decide whether or not to grant full pensions. If it is inconvenient for a large number of committee members to make a decision, the matter can be arbitrated by three people, one nominated by the bureau, one nominated by the relevant consul, and the other nominated jointly by the first two, or appointed by the committee. With such provisions, bureau employees will be protected.

Local News Two

Son Illegally Imprisons His Own Mother

Arising from Embezzlement of Property

Fortunately, the Mother Escaped by Breaking Through the Wall

Fu Zhang, a woman from Pudong, is 67 years old and lives at No. 5 Huazhanjiatang Bay. Recently, she hired Lawyer Dong to sue her eldest son, Fu Atao, at the District Court Prosecutor's Office for attempting to destroy evidence and illegally imprisoning a senior family member. The main points of her indictment are as follows: The plaintiff has four sons: the eldest son Atao (the defendant), the second son Fuxing, the third son Liubao, and the fourth son Qibao. In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, they divided the real estate and land left by their late father, Quan Sheng, according to their respective shares and established a division agreement. However, they had two large ships in Shanghai that specialized in business with foreign firms such as Mei Foo and Ju An, which was quite prosperous. At that time, because Liubao and Qibao were still underage, it was agreed that the eldest son, Atao, and the second son, Fuxing, would manage them. Later, because Fuxing developed an eye disease, Atao was put in charge, with the understanding that after deducting expenses, the accumulated principal and interest would be divided equally among the four shares. Unexpectedly, Atao has been in charge for seven years and has accumulated more than 18,000 yuan in profit, but he has refused to divide it and listens to his wife's words, intending to embezzle it. Therefore, Fuxing, Liubao, and Qibao have filed a lawsuit in your court's civil court (the day before yesterday, the court ordered an out-of-court settlement after the hearing). Unexpectedly, Atao had malicious intentions. On the afternoon of the 20th of this month, at 3:00 PM, while the plaintiff was chatting at her son-in-law Jin Liusheng's house, Atao came to deceive the plaintiff into going to a lawyer's office, urging the plaintiff not to appear in court. The plaintiff was instructed to testify that because both parties were her own children, she should be fair to both sides. Unexpectedly, Atao became malicious and lured the plaintiff to his home for the night. The next morning, his wife and two daughters (the plaintiff's daughter-in-law and granddaughters) escorted the plaintiff to a house in Tangwang Bridge, Chuansha County, for illegal imprisonment. The plaintiff cried and made a lot of noise. In the evening, the plaintiff was escorted to a small room upstairs at Jin Chengkun's house in Yangjing, Pudong, for illegal imprisonment. The door was locked, and the plaintiff's body was not free, which lasted for a whole night. The next day, at around 5:00 AM, the plaintiff saw that the rear wall was broken and that the other guards were still asleep. The plaintiff broke through the wall and escaped, arriving at Liubao's house at 11:00 AM and regaining her freedom. Such illegal imprisonment of a direct relative constitutes a crime under Article 317, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. It is requested that Atao and his wife and daughters be arrested and dealt with according to the law. The prosecutor has ordered that each defendant be summoned to court for verification.

National Anti-Drug Representative Conference Concludes

Publishes Declaration

The National Anti-Drug Representative Conference held its second day of meetings yesterday at the Zhongshe Auditorium on Weihaiwei Road, with more than 100 representatives in attendance. First, Chairman Ge Baohang reported on the election procedures. Then, all the representatives in the venue, for the sake of caution regarding the election of important personnel, decided that the election should be changed to the afternoon. Subsequently, Secretary Li Fengchu of the Anti-Smoking Design Committee, Secretary Zhang Shengcai of the Economic Committee, Deputy Chairman Zhu Qiluo of the Tobacco Committee, Chairman Zhang Zhenliang of the Organization Committee, and Deputy Chairman Wu Zhenduo of the Education and Investigation Committee successively reported on the results of the review of the proposals yesterday. The proposals passed by each group, along with those reserved, were transferred to the Executive Committee for handling, which was unanimously approved by the venue. Then, the representatives voted by secret ballot to elect 15 executive committee members, including Wang Jingqi and Li Denghui, and more than 10 special committee members, including Xiong Xiling and Ma Yinchu. At around 6:00 PM, the closing ceremony of the conference was held. Ge Baohang delivered the closing speech, and the whole assembly dispersed after shouting slogans. The situation of this conference was very good. The proposals passed were all the most important tasks at present. In the future, they will be implemented in order, which will definitely contribute to the domestic anti-drug movement. The conference declaration is excerpted below: At this time, from August 29th to 31st, the 21st year of the Republic of China, the representatives, in view of the rampant drug scourge in the country, which has been spreading endlessly, and that it is not enough to quell the surging tide of opium without gathering the strength of the entire nation, the China National Anti-Drug Association initiated this conference, gathering more than 130 representatives from all over the country to seek strategies for future anti-drug movements. All of them were frank and open, calm and peaceful, and discussed only for the sake of what is right. They scrutinized without being tired of the details, willing to gather the opinions of the majority of groups and individuals to form a concrete plan for anti-drug efforts. A total of more than 90 proposals were submitted, and dozens of groups from all walks of life participated in the discussion. This is a glorious and grand occasion for the conference. The representatives dare to take comfort in this and briefly list them to comfort the people of the country. In the past, the reason why the people's anti-drug movement did not succeed completely was that the key was that the progress of each other was not connected, the voices were not communicated, and people fought on their own, so there was no concentrated force to respond to the rampant drug atmosphere. In the past, the reason why the domestic opium ban was abolished was also that the weakness was that the people were indifferent to this, did not give the authorities appropriate supervision and responsibility, and adopted a supportive attitude, which made those in power able to manipulate the situation and collude with each other. The so-called Chen Yan, who is wise to protect himself and ordinary people do not discuss, is a huge mistake for the people's anti-drug movement. The representatives punished themselves, made up for what they had done before, and felt that to complete the opium ban in our country, we must take the people's anti-drug movement as the main body, and the people's support and supervision is the policy of the government to implement the opium ban. The representatives do not believe that the Chinese people do not have the ability to assist the government, the spirit of unity, the ability to self-determination, and the endowment of civil rights. They dare to start from today, and through the deliberation and cooperation of the representatives from all parties at the meeting, they will use unified strength, orderly steps, and a hundred strategies, and the courage to go forward to carry out a total attack on opium and all anesthetic drugs. They hold the concept that if the drug is in me, I will die, and if I am in the drug, the drug will die. They issue a grand wish to benefit the world. If the poison is still rooted for a day, then the representatives have not fulfilled their responsibility for a day. Now, the voices of opium sales are sometimes loud and sometimes silent. The enemies who destroy the anti-drug work are ambushing around. It is the day when the representatives are restless and staring intently. If the opium ban authorities show an unstable attitude, we will vow to go to the death. If the destroyers have any harmful means, we will defend it with all our strength. We will depend on each other and never forget the sincerity of this day. We will work together and dare to forget the sincerity of this day. We must ensure that after this, every move and every word against drugs will not betray the sincere intention and mission of our participation in the conference today. It is clear above, and it is clear beside. If you break this word, you should abandon it together. The National Anti-Drug Representative Conference hereby declares.

The Garrison Department Burned Opium Yesterday

Held in the Backyard of the Department Yesterday

Commander Dai Ji Personally Supervised

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters burned the opium stored in the Military Law Office of the Headquarters in the open space in the backyard of the Longhua Headquarters at 2:00 PM yesterday. The total amount was more than 1,100 taels. The Municipal Government, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the District Court, the First and Second Special District Courts, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent representatives to supervise. Garrison Commander Dai Ji, Chief of Staff Zhang Xiang, and Adjutant Lin Jing also personally supervised. More than 100 packages of opium were cut open and inspected to ensure that there were no mistakes before they were burned. At that time, Wang Yiji, the Director of the Military Law Office, reported the amount of opium sent by the Public Security Bureau, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Police Department, and other agencies from May 20 to August 22 of this year, one by one. The procedures were extremely cautious and were not completed until 2:30 PM.

Changing Northeast Mail Delivery Methods

Mail from Manchukuo will be verified and treated as underpaid postage. Post offices remain in operation in Heilongjiang Province, such as Daheihe. After the postal blockade of the Northeast, although the Directorate General of Posts has repeatedly revised the methods for delivering mail in the three eastern provinces and the South Manchuria Railway Zone, there were still omissions. Therefore, the Directorate General yesterday, after careful consideration, made further amendments and instructed the Shanghai Postal Administration to comply. Director Zha Peilin issued Bureau Edict No. 1651 yesterday, stating that regarding the methods for mail in the three eastern provinces and the South Manchuria Railway Zone, previous Bureau Edicts No. 1629 and No. 1639 have been notified. Now, according to the order of the Directorate General of Posts, the supplementary methods for mail in the three eastern provinces and the South Manchuria Railway Zone are listed as follows: (Mail from the three eastern provinces or the South Manchuria Railway Zone, posted in Dalian,) All types of mail, with obvious signs on the exterior indicating that they originated from the so-called Manchukuo or the South Manchuria Railway Zone and were forwarded to Dalian for posting, must be subject to a double penalty of postage according to domestic rates, regardless of whether the postage stamps affixed are Japanese postage stamps or not. However, it should be noted that this method of underpaid postage can only be applied to mail whose place of origin is definitely the false Manchukuo or the South Manchuria Railway Zone, without any doubt. If there is any doubt, the mail should not be treated as underpaid postage but should benefit the public. If the recipient sues due to underpaid postage and can prove that the original sending post office was indeed Dalian, the underpaid postage should be waived. (Mail and parcels to the South Manchuria Railway Zone and the Kwantung Leased Territory,) There are no changes to the methods for sending and receiving mail to and from various places in the South Manchuria Railway Zone and the Kwantung Leased Territory. (Mail from Dalian inquiring about mail originating from Manchukuo) For any inquiry from Dalian about ordinary or registered mail originating from the so-called Manchukuo, the receiving office should write the following statement in the answer column of the form: [It has been verified that the item originated from the so-called Manchukuo. Chinese post has no relationship with it, and does not recognize the postage stamps used. The item has been treated as underpaid postage mail without postage.] In addition to the above statement, no other statements are needed. (Mail to various places in Heilongjiang) It has been verified that the following places along the Heilongjiang River are still under the jurisdiction of the National Government. Except for the suspension of remittance and parcel services, the post offices in these places remain open. Daheihe, Aihui, Qikete, Wuyun, Jinshanzhen, Mohe. All mail to these places must be sent to Shanghai, forwarded via Vladivostok, and then transported to Daheihe for delivery, etc. This is hereby ordered to be obeyed and implemented. This order, Zha Peilin, Postal Director.

Two Approvals from the International Trade Association

Agreeing to the principle that exported goods must be labeled with their country of origin.

Returning the import tax on rayon to the Ministry of Finance for consultation.

The China International Trade Association previously requested the Ministry of Industry to specify regulations and order all stores nationwide to label the country of origin of foreign goods they sell; otherwise, they would be severely punished. Now, Approval No. 13285 of the Ministry of Industry has been received, stating that the proposal has been noted. It is considered that it is essential to specify the country of origin and manufacturer of foreign goods sold in the domestic market for identification. Many countries have precedents. China, as a country with import surpluses, is flooded with foreign goods. The original proposal requested that stores be ordered to label the country of origin of foreign goods they sell so that buyers can make informed choices and businesses can have a reference. It has merit. However, at the same time, it is necessary to require that all imported foreign goods be labeled with their country of origin and be strictly inspected by customs to be effective. The association previously submitted the same request to the ministry, which has been sent to the Ministry of Finance for review. The issuance of certificates by consuls abroad is about to be implemented. If only customs restrictions are imposed, foreign merchants will inevitably object, citing consular certification. It is now proposed to consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, ordering consuls abroad to first consider this point when issuing visas and strictly instruct all foreign merchants to clearly label the country of origin, place of origin, or manufacturer on the packaging of goods and to conduct inspections or clearly specify it in the certificate to prevent omissions. Before the aforementioned measures are fully implemented, the request to order all stores nationwide to label the country of origin should be handled properly by chambers of commerce and trade associations in an autonomous manner to the extent possible. If the government specifies laws and strictly enforces them, there may be obstacles. In addition to consulting with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct consuls abroad to pay attention to the conspicuous labeling of the country of origin, place of origin, and manufacturer on the packaging of goods and to strictly limit foreign countries to comply, you are hereby notified, etc. Furthermore, the association's request, forwarded by the Shanghai Electrical Silk Weaving Industry Association, to return the import tax on rayon fabrics and rayon interwoven raw materials exported abroad has also been approved by the Ministry of Industry, stating that it has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review.

Xu Tingyao Inquires About Relief Funds for Huo Qiu

Huo Qiu should have received 60,000 to 70,000 yuan in relief funds for northern Anhui last year.

The county was occupied by bandits, and the funds were not distributed, so they should still exist.

Commander Xu Tingyao of the Fourth Army Division recently recovered Huo Qiu and is planning for local rehabilitation. He repeatedly telegraphed for relief and telegraphed Commissioner Xu Shiying of the Central Relief Commission, stating that the National Government's Flood Relief Committee allocated over one million yuan to northern Anhui last year, to be distributed among 21 counties. Huo Qiu should have received 60,000 to 70,000 yuan, but because the county was occupied by bandits, the funds were not distributed. This relief money should still exist. Please send someone to distribute it as soon as possible, etc. Commissioner Xu, regarding the aforementioned relief funds, inquired with the National Government Disaster Relief Working Group and simultaneously telegraphed Quan Shaowu, Commissioner of the Northern Anhui Relief Office, to investigate how much relief money was allocated to Huo Qiu, to whom the money was given, and whether there was any remaining money, and where it is now. He then received a telegram from Quan Shaowu, stating the facts of the distribution and stating that the money was received by Wang Junbao. As for how it was distributed and whether there was any remaining relief, please inquire with Wang Jun nearby for details. Commissioner Xu then forwarded Quan's telegram and inquired with Wang Jun. It is now heard that Wang Junbaozhai has already responded. The original text of the telegram is disclosed below for reference by those concerned about relief in northern Anhui. Wang Zhuren (i.e., Baozhai) telegraphed, (omitted above) Yesterday, I received a telegram from Bengbu forwarded from Fengyang. I understand everything. On May 22, I went to Bengbu for business, just when the county seat of Huo Qiu was occupied. Refugees from Huo Qiu fled to various places, without food or shelter, and starved to death on the roads. I was heartbroken at the time and immediately thought of ways to provide relief. For several months, I have been running around and consulting with the Northern Anhui Office, receiving a total of 26,000 yuan in relief and 185 tons of relief wheat. After repeated meetings with various fellow villagers, we investigated and distributed emergency relief in Bengbu for the first time with 2,612 and a half bags of American flour (i.e., relief wheat). The second time, we distributed approximately 8,000 yuan in foreign currency (the American hemp was not enough, so it was sold at the current price), 7,000 yuan in Gushi, 4,000 yuan in Yingshang, 8,700 yuan in Chuzhou, Quanjiao, and Laian, 400 yuan in Fuyang, 3,300 yuan in Huaiyuan, Fengtai, Shouxian, Fengyang, and Wuhe, and 1,000 yuan in Hefei, for a total of more than 32,000 yuan. Currently, the distributors in Gushi and Hefei have not returned, so the exact amount cannot be calculated. It is estimated that there are still more than 2,000 yuan left, which is intended to be distributed to the refugees in Huo Qiu who have not escaped. The previous time, I entrusted Commissioner Zhang Zepu to bring the remaining relief money to Huo Qiu for distribution, and he has agreed. In addition to sending a letter to Commander Xu for verification, I hereby reply, Wang Zhuren kowtows.

Estimated value of over 430,000 yuan.

Regarding the case of dividing the accumulated grain and property originally belonging to Shanghai County between the Shanghai Municipality and County, the Real Estate Evaluation Committee has been organized, and Wei Xinyi and others are responsible for surveying and estimating. Significant Decline in Epidemic Situation Last Week

Report by Wu Liande

Wu Liande, Director of the Seaport Quarantine Office and Director of the Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office, issued the 14th Cholera Weekly Report yesterday (August 31). The following is a record: (1) According to records from the end of last week (August 27), a total of only 258 cholera cases were reported in one week, which is a significant decrease compared to the previous week's 347 cases. The cholera epidemic has been greatly reduced. The locations where cholera was found last week are listed below:

Area Cases Deaths

Shanghai City 75 2

International Settlement 20 (including 3 foreigners) 12 (including 2 foreigners)

French Concession 92 (including 1 foreigner) 3

Unknown Area 2 0

Total for Last Week 258 (including 4 foreigners) 17 (including 2 foreigners)

Previous Total 3714 (including 66 foreigners) 272 (including 17 foreigners)

Total 3972 (including 70 foreigners) 290 (including 19 foreigners)

(2) As of the end of last week, approximately 4,000 cases of cholera have been discovered, including 70 foreigners, with 290 deaths, including 19 foreigners. From this, it can be inferred that 3,902 Chinese people have contracted cholera, with 271 deaths, meaning the cholera mortality rate for Chinese people is 6.9%. 70 foreigners contracted cholera, with 19 deaths, meaning the cholera mortality rate for foreigners is 27.1%. (3) The cholera epidemic in Shanghai is indeed showing a trend of disappearing. This can be inferred from the recent situation of the clinics in various epidemic hospitals. The beds in the hospitals are mostly vacant, especially in the Xizang Road Epidemic Hospital. The hospital can accommodate more than 3,000 beds, and since the cholera outbreak, the number of patients treated has been countless. (4) According to reports from various seaports, the cholera trend in those ports is also showing the same reduction. For example, for the weekend of August 20, Xiamen reported 97 cholera cases, with 21 deaths, Guangzhou 7 cases, with 2 deaths, Hankou 113 cases, with 20 deaths, Shantou 49 cases, with 11 deaths, Tanggu 2 cases, with 1 death, Tianjin 1 case, and Nanjing reported 93 cases, with 7 deaths for the weekend of August 27. (5) Qingdao, despite strict prevention, was also invaded by cholera on July 11. As of August 20, a total of 52 cholera cases have been discovered, with 10 deaths, compared to 18 cases and 4 deaths in the previous week. (6) Autumn has arrived, the epidemic has decreased, and those who serve in cholera epidemic hospitals and laboratories or run around providing treatment in cholera epidemic areas can now rest after their hard work in the past. Shanghai is a large city with a large population, and this tiger epidemic was able to pass smoothly, achieving such good results. This is all thanks to the proper handling by the health authorities. Therefore, although there is a large area with a population of 3.5 million, the cholera mortality rate is only 7%, which is truly rare and worthy of research.

Shanghai Electrical Silk Weaving Association Endorses Silk Fabric Appraisal Method

Raw material registration will be organized, and the association will be responsible for guaranteeing it.

The Shanghai Electrical Silk Weaving Industry Association has a positive opinion regarding the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry's silk fabric appraisal method. It has specifically notified its members that raw material registration will begin on September 1, and appraisal will be implemented as soon as the procedures are completed. The original letter is recorded below: Dear Sirs, we have received a letter from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, stating that in order to promote domestically produced silk fabrics and facilitate the public's understanding of quality, our bureau plans to implement silk fabric appraisal in the shortest possible time. We are sending you six articles of the appraisal rules, mimeographed, for your reference. It has been found that silk fabric appraisal is indeed the only way to prove domestic goods, and the bureau's stamping of seals on both ends of the fabric will further facilitate public recognition of quality. The method is good and well-intentioned. At a time when inferior goods are filling the market and causing confusion, appraising silk fabrics to prove domestic goods is a matter of great urgency. All of our members should enthusiastically accept it. Therefore, our association has convened an executive committee meeting, unanimously approved, and decided that before the bureau implements the appraisal, our association must first organize the raw material registration work for the members. After this procedure is completed, we can complete the request form and request appraisal in accordance with the rules, guaranteed by our association. It is scheduled from September 1st to 5th as the period for registering raw materials in stock. All members must, within these five days, combine the warp and weft raw materials in stock as of August 31st, including those on the machine and sizing silk, verify them, fill out a form, and send it to the association. From September 1st onwards, future purchases of raw materials must be reported to the association before the transaction is completed, and the association will fill out the certificate for registration. Otherwise, if they are concealed and not reported, the association will not be responsible for any external inquiries in the future. This matter is related to promoting domestic goods, business interests, and has a great impact. Please pay close attention and do not delay, lest you regret it later. In addition to the attached copy of the appraisal rules, inventory raw material registration form, and volunteer form, we are sending this letter accordingly. Please refer to it. Attached (Silk Fabric Appraisal Rules of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry) Article 1: In order to promote domestically produced silk fabrics and facilitate the public's understanding of their quality, this bureau has specially formulated these rules to implement silk fabric appraisal. Article 2: The products of silk weaving factories within the borders of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces must be appraised by this bureau to determine whether they are purely domestic genuine silk fabrics or interwoven fabrics of genuine silk and rayon, etc. After the appraisal, this bureau will stamp seals on both ends of the fabric to prove it. After the silk fabric is appraised by this bureau, when it is rolled, one end with the seal should be exposed to the outside so that buyers can easily recognize it. Article 3: In addition to sending personnel to be stationed in various refineries to carry out appraisal procedures, each factory may send its products to this bureau for appraisal. Article 4: Each factory requesting appraisal of silk fabrics must fill out a request form with a duplicate, and report to this bureau with a guarantee from the industry association. Those who transport their products to the bureau for appraisal will be implemented in order of priority. Article 5: This bureau will charge a handling fee of one cent per piece for appraising silk fabrics, regardless of their quality and price. Article 6: These rules will be implemented from the date of promulgation by bureau order upon approval by the bureau.

Judgment in the Yuanshenghao Appeal Case

Defendants Sentenced to Imprisonment

Yuanshenghao is a well-known securities firm in Shanghai. The general manager, Shi Zian, colluded with the former manager of the China Exchange Bank, Tian Hongnian, to embezzle and misappropriate funds, resulting in a loss of over 240,000 yuan. At the end of last year, shareholders Yu Shouzheng, Luo Kunxiang, and others filed a lawsuit in the first instance, and the verdict was rendered a month ago, establishing the crime of breach of trust. However, only a fine of 1,000 yuan was imposed on each of them. The plaintiffs were dissatisfied and appealed, while the defendants considered the fine a victory and made no indication of any kind. Judge Yu Hua presided over the case. In addition to slightly questioning the facts determined in the original trial, he also summoned the managing director of the China Exchange Bank to testify. The bank elected Yao Yong as their representative to testify in court, stating that the loan to Yuansheng was entirely the decision of Tian Hongnian alone, and the board of directors had never agreed to it beforehand, which was quite unfavorable to the defendants. The appellate trial consisted of two court sessions and then declared the debate closed. The plaintiffs' lawyers were Zhang Shizhao, Dong Kang, and Peng Yuanxun, while the defendants' defense lawyers were Yuan Yang'an and Zhu Fengchi. The arguments on both sides were very激烈 (intense/heated). Yesterday (i.e., August 31), at 8:00 AM, Judge Yu ascended to the first courtroom and announced the verdict, rescinding the sentencing portion of the original verdict. Shi Zian was sentenced to imprisonment for continuous breach of trust and fined 500 yuan. Tian Hongnian was sentenced to six months' imprisonment for joint breach of trust and fined 300 yuan. If they fail to pay, they will be subject to imprisonment at a rate of three yuan per day. This sensational breach of trust case has now come to an end in its second stage. Lawyer Zhang's appeal, regarding the overly lenient sentencing, contained a narrative tracing the origins of jurisprudence, which people referred to as an ancient-style pleading. A small newspaper published a short excerpt, and readers were surprised, saying that the citation of sources in the pleading was unprecedented. Lawyer Yuan Yang'an attacked in court, saying that Lawyer Zhang was abusing logic and not sticking to the facts, and that his thinking was outdated, constantly referring to the Three Dynasties, which seemed to be legal thinking that should not exist in the 20th century. This kind of legal battle writing, which is not often seen, is what the public is eager to see. Lawyer Dong's concise statement also contained many insightful remarks, such as saying that criminal law fraud, breach of trust, and general embezzlement are all treated the same, ending with a fine of 1,000 yuan, which is to give the judge the power to use it, not to leave it for perfunctory use. Moreover, the penalty of a fine, according to the explanatory memorandum of the 46th article of the Second Amendment, has been recognized as a minor penalty. This book has the same effect as this law, and the court cannot be unaware of it.] The wording is cold and refined, and deserves to be called a masterpiece. Due to the complexity of the words, I apologize for not recording them all.

Abusing Maidservant Results in Eight Months Imprisonment

Xu Changxian, a 50-year-old man from Pudong residing in a bungalow at the corner of Linqing Road and Hejian Road, adopted a nine-year-old girl named Ju Mei as his daughter last autumn for one hundred yuan in his hometown of Datuan. However, the girl suffered from enuresis, leading to Xu's frequent beatings. Early in the morning, around six o'clock, Xu beat Ju Mei again for no reason, causing injuries all over her body and swelling and bruising around her eyes. Ju Mei cried at the door, and a neighbor, Song Wanye from Jiangbei, couldn't bear to see it and reported it to Chinese Constable No. 848 at the nearby station. The constable arrested Xu and took him and Ju Mei to the Yangshupu Police Station. The police chief ordered Xu's detention, and Ju Mei was sent to the Jiliang Institute to await questioning. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Fourth Criminal Court of the First Special District. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, recounted the previous events and requested a severe sentence. Ju Mei, when questioned, was pale and emaciated, with severely bruised and swollen eyes. She kept her head down and dared not speak. The court asked how her eyes were injured, but she remained silent. The court told her not to be afraid, and she said she had been beaten with fists. A female staff member from the Jiliang Institute slightly rolled up her clothes, revealing severe scars on the girl's back and legs, which was heartbreaking to see. Xu confessed that because the girl wet the bed, he had only slightly scolded her, claiming her eyes were injured from bumping into something in her sleep. He had spent one hundred yuan to adopt her as an heir, hoping she would take care of him in his old age. He presented the purchase document and asked for consideration. Judge Fu Lin questioned him, stating that he had a wife and should not have brutally beaten the girl if she had done wrong, treating her like an animal. He added that if the girl grew up, he would make her a prostitute to make a living. The defendant lowered his head without a word, pleading for leniency. The police lawyer Zhang then stated that Ju Mei did not want to go home and wanted to study at the Jiliang Institute. Judge Fu then sentenced Xu Changxian to eight months of imprisonment as a warning. Ju Mei was sent to the Jiliang Institute for care.

Verdict in Illegal Possession of Firearms Case

According to a tip from Chen Sanbao, a Tongzhou native, to the French Concession Police's special task force, Chen Baoyuan and Zhao Haihai, both from Tongzhou, who rented and pulled rickshaws on Lujiabang Road in the South City, and Wang Xiaofu, from Jiangyin, who lived at No. 8, Renmei Lane, West New Bridge Street in the French Concession, were illegally possessing firearms and had committed robberies in the French Concession. The detectives arrested Chen and the other two and found a pistol in a pile of bricks outside Chen Baoyuan's house. They were taken to the Second Special District Court for questioning. Chen and the other two claimed they had never committed robbery and were ordered to be detained for investigation. Later, the police found out that Chen and the other two had a feud with Zhang Laobao, a Tongzhou native who also pulled a rickshaw and lived at No. 6 Lujiabang Road. Zhang had hidden the gun in the brick pile and incited Chen Sanbao to falsely report them. It was confirmed that Zhang and Chen had framed them. Zhang and Chen were arrested and taken to court for interrogation. The police charged Zhang and Chen with false accusation under Article 180 of the law. The court ordered Chen Baoyuan and the other two to be released. Zhang and Chen were held for sentencing. Yesterday, Judge Li Changnian presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Zhang Laobao to three years' imprisonment for falsely accusing others with the intent to subject them to criminal penalties, and six months' imprisonment for possessing military firearms, to be served concurrently for a total of three years and two months. Chen Sanbao was sentenced to one year and two months' imprisonment for falsely accusing others with the intent to subject them to criminal penalties. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed would be counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. The pistol was confiscated.

Private Minting of Copper "Double Horns" Sentences Imposed

Dai Yu Gui, Zhou Xuejia, Xu Changshan, and Zheng Guizeng, all from various regions, were arrested in Yuezhou Road No. 322 and Xinkang Li No. 1131, Xin Zha Road, for privately minting copper "double horns" (a type of coin) and circulating them in the market for profit. Huishan Police Detective Huang Fugen and Ji Peijin successively arrested them and seized more than 270 counterfeit coins, as well as molds, iron pots, iron rivets, alum, and other materials. Suspects Xu Xueming and a woman, Zhou Liu, were also taken into custody and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the Fourth Criminal Court and sentenced Dai Yu Gui, Zhou Xuejia, Xu Changshan, and Zheng Guizeng to seven years and six months of imprisonment each. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed would be counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. The counterfeit coins and evidence were confiscated. Xu Xueming and Zhou Liu were found not guilty and released immediately after the police lawyer Zhang waived the right to appeal.

One Life Lost for One Dollar

A Mediator's Hard Fate

Barge owners Chen Linhu and Wang Meifu, sailing together on a boat, collided with Ye Shenglin's barge near the Bund Beijing Road pier at 9:30 PM on the 23rd of last month. Chen and Wang's boat suffered minor damage, so they demanded compensation. After negotiation, Ye agreed to pay one dollar but did not have the money on hand. Gong Ronghua, a fellow barge owner acting as a mediator, agreed to lend the money. He gave one dollar to Ye to pass on to Wang. However, Wang later secretly asked Gong for the money directly. Gong replied that the money had already been given to Ye, so he could not pay again, leading to an argument. Wang and Chen violently assaulted Gong, who could not defend himself and was injured. However, the two did not stop and tried to drag Gong ashore for further beating. In the dark, Gong suddenly lost his footing and fell into the Huangpu River. Seeing that a life had been taken, Chen and Wang fled. Although Gong knew how to swim, he was seriously injured and unable to struggle, resulting in drowning. Trying to resolve a dispute, he lost his own life. Ye Shenglin immediately reported the incident to Gong's wife, Sun, who then reported it to the General Police Station, requesting the arrest of the perpetrators Wang Meifu and Chen Linhu. Meanwhile, they tried to recover the body. Detective Ni Jiaxin arrested Wang and Chen. The body was finally found on the 25th and taken to the Fielun Road morgue. The coroner confirmed that death was due to drowning after being beaten. The family was instructed to collect the body. The police yesterday sent Wang and Chen to the First Special District Court. Judge Shen interrogated them, and the police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, requested that the two defendants be punished according to Article 294 of the Criminal Law. Gong's wife, Gong Sun, stated that she had a 70-year-old mother-in-law and a two-year-old child who depended on her husband for support and requested that the defendants be ordered to pay compensation of 1,000 yuan. However, the two defendants only agreed to pay more than 100 yuan, stating that they could not afford a larger amount. After arguments between the defendants' lawyer and the police lawyer, Judge Shen ordered the defendants to be detained and set a date for sentencing.

Boat Girl Drowns

Zhao, a boatman from Suzhou, had a 17-year-old daughter who had been promised in marriage and was scheduled to marry in the first month of the next spring. In order to buy her dowry, the girl accompanied her mother on a boat to Shanghai. The boat was moored at the public pier on the south embankment of the old garbage bridge on the Suzhou River. Yesterday (the 31st), at 12:30 PM, during a heavy rainstorm, Zhao's daughter went ashore to shop. However, the gangplank was slippery, and she lost her footing and fell into the river. The tide was high at the time. Zhao and the boat crew immediately tried to rescue her, and they finally retrieved her body at 1:30 PM. They carried her ashore and tried to resuscitate her, but she had been in the water too long and could not be revived. Her body was laid on the bow of the boat, and her mother and others wept bitterly.

Ning Shao Steamer Line Revises Tips Starting Today

Adhering to Ministry Orders to Collect 20% of Ticket Price

It has been observed that the tips given to the stewards by passengers on various commercial steamers traveling between Shanghai and Ningbo often equal the ticket price, greatly exceeding the fare itself. Although these tips are supposedly voluntary, they have become a customary practice. Given the current difficult economic situation, this burden on passengers is excessively heavy. The Ning Shao Steamer Line Company, recognizing this issue, has decided to implement a new policy starting from September 1st. Stewards' tips on the new Ning Shao steamers will be uniformly set at 20% of the ticket price, in accordance with Ministry orders. This restriction has been officially announced to all stewards on the new Ning Shao line.

Bank of China Inspection Report

54th Examination

The 54th inspection report of the Shanghai Bank of China Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members and accountants, in accordance with the committee's rules, inspected the special reserve of the Shanghai Bank of China's head office for banknotes issued and redeemed by affiliated banks. The 54th inspection was conducted on August 28, 1932, and the Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance joined in the inspection. The results of the inspection are listed below: Total amount of banknotes issued: 95,347,171 yuan, including: Amount issued by the head office: 52,500,760 yuan; Amount used by affiliated banks: 17,617,687 yuan; Amount used by various banks and firms: 25,221,824 yuan. Except for the part used by various banks and firms, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, the inspection of the affiliated banks is as follows: Amount issued by the head office and used by affiliated banks: 70,125,247 yuan; Reserve for banknotes issued and used by affiliated banks: 70,125,247 yuan, including: Cash reserve: 43,062,006.50 yuan; Guarantee reserve: 27,063,340.05 yuan. The above two items, with a cash reserve accounting for 60% and a guarantee reserve accounting for 40%, were all verified without error. In accordance with Article 5 of the rules, this formal report is submitted. August 28, 1932. Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance; Wang Yansong, Fei Yunqing, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce; Xu Xinliu, Wang Zhixin, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association; Fu Songnian, Li Jisheng, representatives of the Shanghai Money Dealers Association; Wang Wenzhi, Zheng Boren, representatives of the banks and firms issuing banknotes; Ye Zhuodang, Xu Jilong, Zhou Zongliang, Li Zhilian, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the Bank of China; Accountant Wang Zikang.

The Busyness of the Zhabei Epidemic Hospital

Since the Zhabei War, countless poor people have died from epidemics. Although autumn has arrived and the epidemic has subsided somewhat, malaria and dysentery have followed, and various other diseases have arisen, making life difficult for the poor. Wu Xingya, the director of the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, and other enthusiastic philanthropists in Shanghai, such as Du Yuesheng, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, and Wang Xiaolai, organized the Zhabei Epidemic Hospital. After several planning sessions, they found the site of the Guangdong Hospital on Tiantong'an Road, which had spacious buildings and a large scale. After renovations, it was completely new, with orderly arrangements and layout. The patients' clothing and bedding were all new, and the rooms were clean and well-ventilated. They also invited the famous Shanghai doctor Zhu Yaxiong to serve as the medical director, responsible for the medical operations. The doctors were all well-educated and stationed in the hospital day and night, making the medical work extremely busy. The patients who recovered and were discharged were all grateful and happy. This is truly a blessing for the patients.

Scheduled Memorial Service for Zhou Shiying

Zhou Shiying, the director of the Shanghai Anlao (Peaceful Aging) Home, was a native of Ningbo. He was honest, thrifty, benevolent, and generous. He used all of his private property to found the Anlao Home in Nanxiang, providing care for helpless elderly women and saving countless lives. Unfortunately, the home was bombed by Japanese troops this spring, killing five elderly women. Zhou was overwhelmed with grief, and his old illness worsened, leading to his death on May 28 of this year, at the age of 55. After Zhou's death, Tian'an Church members Niu Huisheng, Niu Huilin, and pastor You Jianren initiated a memorial service, scheduled for 3:00 PM on the 3rd of this month at Tian'an Church on Shandong Road. Gifts from friends and church members will be collected and used for the home's expenses. Zhou had a wide circle of friends and acquaintances, and many are expected to attend the memorial service.

Original Text of the Labor-Management Agreement of Huachang Splints Factory

Shanghai Splint Industry Union, Agreement between Labor and Capital at Huachang Match Splint Factory. (1) The factory recognizes the union's right to represent the workers. (2) For workers in the wood stacking department, wages will be increased by 2.50 yuan for those earning between 7 and 8 yuan, 2 yuan for those earning between 8 and 10 yuan, and 1.50 yuan for all those earning above 10 yuan. This increase will be implemented once a year on June 1st, up to a maximum of 16 yuan. Carpenters will receive their usual wages. A double bonus will be paid in December. Other departments will receive a bonus of one yuan at the end of the year. (3) Workers in the wood stacking department will not have their wages deducted for sick leave. For personal leave, the deducted wages will be divided into two periods, the end of June and the end of December, and distributed to the working workers. The number of workers taking personal leave is limited to five. (4) Workers in the wood stacking department will not have their wages deducted for marriage or funeral leave (limited to parents, self, and wife). The leave is limited to two weeks, with full wages paid. Wages will be deducted for leave exceeding this period. Female workers on the cart will receive 10 days of marriage leave with a daily wage of 20 cents. This does not apply to funeral leave. (5) Female workers who have worked for more than nine months will receive six weeks of maternity leave, with a daily allowance of 20 cents. (6) All seven government-mandated holidays will be observed. Workers in the wood stacking department will receive full wages. Male workers in other departments will receive an allowance of 45 cents, and female workers will receive an allowance of 35 cents, to be collected by the union. (7) The factory will cover medical expenses for workers injured on duty and will provide a daily allowance of 45 cents for splint department workers and full wages for wood stacking department workers during the medical leave period, based on a doctor's certificate. This does not apply to injuries not incurred on duty. (8) The factory will provide a compensation of 150 yuan for workers who are injured or killed on duty. (9) The factory will provide food and lodging for workers in the wood stacking department. Workers who voluntarily live outside the factory are free to do so, but the factory will not provide an allowance. (10) Supervisors and foremen must not abuse workers or arbitrarily deduct wages and must not dismiss workers without good reason. (11) The factory will provide the union with 20 yuan per month for labor welfare, to be collected by the union. (12) The number of workers in the wood stacking department will remain the same. (13) Each planer cart will receive a daily subsidy of 10 cents. When making short tree trunks, the factory will provide subsidies calculated at the average wage. Each cutting cart will receive a daily subsidy of 7 cents per dollar of polished money. The factory will bear the cost of carrying the basket. The supervisor and the planer cart workers will jointly decide on the hiring, firing, wage increases, and wage decreases of the female workers on the cart. (14) The tools for the planer and cutting carts will remain the same. Other tools will be paid at 70% of the original price. (15) For the stem department, 20 cents will be paid per 100 catties of imitation poplar and American poplar. This includes the wages of female workers and child laborers on the cart. (16) For the splint department, the existing original price will be increased by 17.5% per 10,000 splints. (17) The union will be fully responsible for guaranteeing the membership of workers in the wood stacking department. New workers entering the factory must have a proper introduction and submit an application and guarantee form. They can only work in the factory after the factory deems them qualified. (18) If the weather conditions prevent work, the workers in the wood stacking department should remain in the factory to provide services. If necessary or when the tide rises and falls for loading and unloading goods, it must be handled at any time, regardless of the time of day, and no excuses can be made. (19) During working hours, workers must obtain permission from the supervisor to leave the factory for legitimate reasons. (20) If any department lacks raw materials, male workers will receive a monthly meal allowance of 8 yuan, and female workers making long strips will receive a monthly meal allowance of 6 yuan. (21) The female workers on the cart who are making long strips will each receive a monthly meal allowance of 6 yuan (same as Article 20). (22) The stem making department will continue to work as usual when it rains. The splint making department will work as usual when it rains if manpower permits. (23) This agreement will take effect after it is signed by both labor and management. (24) This agreement is valid for one year. It can be renewed if both parties agree. August 26, 1932. Factory representative: Shao Gaoxiang; Union representatives: Standing Director Yan Quanrong, Director Chen Shugui; Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters representative: He Yuanming; Fifth District Party Headquarters representative: Zhang Sheng.

My client states that he had already transferred the handling of matters relating to the Taihe Street house to the legal firm of Youni Gan, and that he was not involved in the recent dispute. Therefore, the report in your newspaper is not in accordance with the facts. I am writing to you at his request to seek a correction, so that the truth may be known. Sincerely, Lawyer Liu Gui, August 31.

Sincerely, The Joint Office of the District Branches of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association, Hongkou District, August 31.
