Education News

Important News

Jiangsu Education Department Promulgates Integrated Teaching and Guidance Measures

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, in order to implement character education and rectify academic conduct, has specially formulated integrated teaching and guidance measures to reform the separate systems of teaching and guidance, and to correct the concept that teachers neglect guidance. However, as these measures are innovative and involve finances and organization, they cannot be fully implemented according to the ideal plan immediately. Therefore, two types of measures have been formulated: preliminary implementation measures and pilot implementation measures. The preliminary measures will be based on the existing organization of each school and will be implemented immediately. For the pilot measures, a small number of schools will be designated for trial implementation. After evaluating the results, they will be implemented universally in the coming year. The two sets of measures are detailed below.

Preliminary Implementation Measures for Integrated Teaching and Guidance in Jiangsu Provincial and County Secondary Schools

Article 1: General Principles. Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has formulated these measures with reference to the existing organization of each school to promote the preliminary implementation of integrated teaching and guidance in provincial and county secondary schools. Article 2: The principles for formulating these measures are as follows: (1) Gradually reform the separate systems of teaching and guidance; (2) Encourage teachers and students to live together and emphasize the influence of character; (3) Train students' thinking based on Party principles and using teaching materials from all subjects; (4) Correct the concept that teachers neglect guidance responsibilities. Article 3: The principals of secondary schools are responsible for earnestly implementing, leading, supervising, and evaluating these measures. Organization. Article 4: Each school shall divide students in each grade into groups of 20 to 30 students (each grade with more than 30 students shall be divided into two groups). Each group shall have a tutor, and each grade shall have a chief tutor. The existing guidance counselors shall be abolished. The tutors of each group shall be full-time teachers, and the chief tutors shall be concurrently held by the heads of each department. If the number of heads is insufficient, the principal shall select them from the tutors. Article 5: Full-time teachers have the obligation to serve as tutors. Those who serve as chief tutors may receive an additional monthly salary. Article 6: Each school shall establish a guidance conference to decide on all training matters. The organization shall be separately determined by each school with reference to the outline of secondary school organization. Article 7: Each school should establish a general office for teaching and guidance, but high schools and junior high schools may establish separate offices. Duties. Article 8: The chief tutors, under the direction of the guidance conference, are responsible for the following tasks: (1) Living with the students of the respective grade in terms of diet, daily life, work, recreation, and rest; (2) Guiding and observing the students of the respective grade in terms of conduct, thought, and academic performance at all times; (3) Participating in and guiding students' various extracurricular activities and self-government organizations; (4) Holding grade-level talks once every two weeks and individual talks at any time; (5) Convening all tutors and teachers of the respective grade to discuss the method of linking teaching and guidance in the grade once a month; (6) Attending the office to approve student leave requests and handle occasional matters among students in the grade; (7) Compiling and organizing the academic and behavioral reports prepared by the tutors of each group each month, reviewing the students' life notebooks in the grade, and filling out the grade report cards at the end of each semester; (8) Managing matters such as discipline, service, hygiene, cleanliness, and attendance observation of students in the grade. Article 9: The tutors, under the direction of the guidance conference and in consultation with the chief tutors, shall perform the following tasks: (1) Convening group talks with students in each group once a week and individual talks at any time; (2) Closely observing and guiding students' words and actions, and filling out the group reports once a month, the grade's chief tutor, [if] necessary, must report; (3) Guiding students in the grade outside, [in addition to] the extracurricular activities and self-government affairs of each group; (4) Leading students in self-study; (5) Attending guidance conferences and various school meetings and assemblies. Article 10: The service status of the chief tutors and tutors shall be earnestly assessed by the principal and reported to the Education Department for record at the end of each semester. Conference. Article 11: The guidance conference shall be held once a month. In addition to deciding on the matters originally stipulated in the outline of secondary school organization, it shall also decide on the following matters: (1) Planning the progress of integrated teaching and guidance; (2) Deciding on training programs and their implementation methods; (3) Deciding on the central work of each period of training based on the program, and reviewing the results of the implementation of the central work of the previous period; (4) Reviewing various regulations and forms regarding training matters; (5) Discussing major occasional matters concerning students; (6) Reviewing student report cards at the end of each semester; (7) Deciding on the method of using teaching materials to realize integrated teaching and guidance; (8) Discussing matters submitted by the principal for discussion and matters requested by other conferences; (9) Stipulating guidance matters for student self-government and extracurricular activities at the beginning of each semester, and assigning guidance personnel; (10) Other matters related to training. Article 12: In order to [ensure] the connection of training in each grade and [to ensure] [each] week, the guidance director shall convene a chief tutor conference once, chaired by the guidance director. When the guidance director is on leave, the principal may designate a chief tutor to act as his agent. The attendees of the chief tutor conference shall be the principal, the guidance director, and all chief tutors. When necessary, relevant tutors or other personnel may be invited to attend. Article 13: The main items for discussion at the chief tutor conference are as follows: (1) Reporting on the actual situation of implementing the central work in each grade and exchanging opinions to determine the steps to be taken this week; (2) Handling matters of mutual relations between grades and discussing all difficult problems in training; (3) Drawing up lists of students' seating arrangements and groupings for meals, accommodation, self-study, etc. at the beginning of each semester; (4) Discussing other matters that should be suggested regarding teaching and guidance. Article 14: Each school shall separately formulate detailed plans and rules for the implementation of these measures and submit them to the Department for approval before implementation. Article 15: Each school shall submit a detailed report on the results of the implementation of these measures at the end of each semester to the Education Department for verification. Article 16: These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Education Department and reported to the Provincial Government for record.

Comparative General Report on the Situation of Municipal and Provincial People's Schools in the 20th Year

(1)

School Teaching Matters

The Ministry of Education compiled a general report on the situation of people's schools in the provinces and cities in the 20th year. A brief report was published earlier. The comparative general report on school teaching matters is extracted below.

(I) Year of Establishment: Year 8 of the Republic: Zhejiang, Shanxi; Year 13: Sichuan, Chahar; Year 14: Suiyuan, Gansu; Year 16: Nanjing, Jiangsu, Henan, Shaanxi; Year 17: Hunan, Shandong, Shanghai, Fujian; Year 18: Beiping, Jiangxi, Anhui, Qingdao, Guangdong, Rehe; Year 19: Hubei; Year 20: Yunnan, Ningxia, Xinjiang, Weihai (Zhejiang and Shanxi, established in Year 8, were the earliest. Yunnan, etc., established in Year 20, were the latest. The most were established in Year 18.)

(II) Current System: 8 regions have established ordinary people's schools and also have senior schools or senior classes (Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Sichuan, Shanghai, Xinjiang).

(III) Faculty and Staff: (1) Concurrent positions in 24 provinces and cities, full-time in 1 province (Gansu); (2) Qualifications: mostly graduates of secondary schools, with a small number of local social education institution personnel or graduates of elementary schools holding concurrent positions; (3) Remuneration: completely voluntary in 2 regions, 4 yuan monthly salary in 2 regions, within 10 yuan in 6 regions, 2 yuan to 28 yuan in 1 region, 6 yuan to 16 yuan in 1 region, 12 yuan in 4 regions, 15 yuan in 1 region, 6 yuan to 40 yuan in 1 region, 20 yuan in 4 regions, 20 yuan to 40 yuan in 1 region, 20 yuan to 50 yuan in 1 region, 45 yuan (full-time teachers) in 1 region. The average of all items is 16 yuan and 10 cents; (4) Service situation: According to reports from various provinces and cities, most are still working hard and doing their duty.

(IV) Students (1) Methods of Encouraging Enrollment: Ten regions rely solely on literacy campaigns, eight regions use both door-to-door individual persuasion, and other regions use usual publicity, lectures, and costume publicity. One region uses individual home visits, or holds meetings with students' families and encourages students to persuade each other. One region, in addition to holding literacy campaigns, uses considerable warning methods. One region persuades and urges transmission by the district and township offices in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau. One region, in addition to holding literacy campaigns, uses other methods. Some have provisions for compulsory enrollment methods (2) Coeducation in 1 region (Henan), coeducation in 23 regions (Sichuan separates boys and girls), schools exclusively for boys in 1 region. Therefore, the percentage of boys' schools: Xinjiang 100%, Rehe 98%, Shandong 95.2%, Shanghai 44%, average 81.8%. Opinions on Sending Zheng Zhaojia to the Americas

In order to revive the Chinese tennis world

Please invite Mr. Zheng to go to California

Support Lin Baohua to go to the United States together

Hope for unanimous advocacy

Friends who care about the tennis situation in Shanghai are unanimous in saying that Zheng Zhaojia is Shanghai's future champion and will be China's first national player in the future. However, with Mr. Zheng's talent, staying in Shanghai for a long time will definitely not make much progress. Lin Qiu is a precedent. Therefore, in order to revive Chinese tennis and restore the glory of the eighth Far Eastern Games, everyone unanimously advocates inviting Mr. Zheng to go to the United States. Lin Baohua also wrote a very thorough letter, which was published in the Mainland Report. Whether or not to take this up, this is our opinion.

California is the Most Appropriate

Of course, needless to say, with Mr. Zheng's talent, if he can live in the United States for one or two years, his technical progress will be greatly improved through the influence of various famous players. For the sake of reviving the Chinese tennis world, it is necessary to invite Mr. Zheng to go to the United States. Moreover, California is the center and birthplace of American tennis stars.

Don't Want Mr. Zheng to Sacrifice His Studies

However, Mr. Zheng is still in school, and he must not sacrifice all his studies in order to become a special tennis player. Therefore, the most appropriate way is to go to California to study for a few years, just like Barnes, who is a student at the University of Southern California.

Hope the 협진회 Will Rise Up and Advocate

We don't know about Mr. Zheng's family situation. Going to the Americas like this will of course be a heavy financial burden. Today, when China cannot take care of anything, it is impossible to ask the government for help. Therefore, I think friends who love tennis, are enthusiastic about sports, and hope that China can win some honor in sports, everyone should rise up and express their advocacy, and the中華全國體育협진회 can also rise up and take the lead.

Support Lin Baohua to go together

If it becomes a reality, Mr. Zheng will go. The next question is this. However, creating a Zheng Zhaojia, for example, if you want to participate in the Davis Cup, a single army will not form a brigade. To go to Wimberton alone, I am afraid there will be very few achievements. Therefore, we very much hope that Lin Baohua will go together.

Lin Baohua Also Has Hope

Many people oppose Lin because his skills have regressed. The real reason for the regression is that he can't find the opportunity to practice. Mr. Lin is only twenty-six years old now. With his talent, he is naturally a promising person. Moreover, Mr. Zheng is his student, and the success of their doubles cooperation this summer makes us firmly believe that Mr. Lin has the necessary conditions to go together. We must go to the active side. Negativity, in other words, is suicide.

Soliciting Public Opinion

As for the trip to the United States by Mr. Zheng and Mr. Lin, some people agree to ask the government authorities and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for help. This is our proposal. How to proceed? I hope that friends who pay attention to this issue will publish their opinions and everyone will promote the realization of this matter. The opportunity cannot be missed again.

Free Talk

A Record of the Leshan Hall

— Xu Jingxian

I once recited a poem by the early Qing Dynasty artist Mo Jingdao, which said: [This joy is extraordinary joy, the sound of the bell shakes the four seas. Seven thousand years pass in an instant, ninety thousand miles of sailing. The sun shines brightly in the mid-heaven, the stars shine brightly at dawn. There is nothing else to offer joy, but a volume of gospel.] This kind of poetic realm, what is called Leshan Hall, seems to resemble it!

Leshan Hall is where Mr. Ma Xiangbo, a ninety-three-year-old, currently resides. The address is in Xujiahui, facing the former residence of Xu Guangqi of Ming Dynasty, looking at each other from afar, like neighbors. Sixty years ago, the old man was over thirty years old. In addition to lecturing and discussing Tao, he was engaged in observing celestial phenomena. Later, he went to serve in Korea, and was sent to Dongying, visited North America, and returned to Europe. He returned to his parents' country to ask about politics and promote learning. He is old! It is rare for life to reach seventy years in ancient times. The villagers also broadcast as a beautiful talk. I still remember the famous Roman Ji Zailu said in the book on old age that [old age can be calm and pure, then it must be gentle and without offense, such as Plato at the age of eighty-one, still writing until his death. Isocrates at the age of ninety-four, also wrote books without stopping, and his teacher Georgeya at the age of one hundred and seven, still tirelessly taught people.] I also remember that Mr. Wu Zhihui wished the owner of Leshan Hall: [Get the thickness of heaven and earth, should live to be 18,000 years old, only after twice 1%.] This can show that heaven is generous to the ancients and not thin to the present people.

Dr. Ling, constitutional elder of Shen Bao, asked for words and once recorded the sayings of Ma Xiangbo, an old man of ninety-three; now, due to business, he asked me to continue it: I will record what I have heard. If there is any error, the responsibility lies with the reporter!

Wishing the [Transformation] of Free Talk!

— Yang Zheng

Free [Talk] Talk [Freedom]

[Freedom] The word in China, which had not been Europeanized and closed to the outside world, was of course not the modern [freedom] that is taught together with [equality]; it only carried the meaning of [casual]. Literally, the three words [Free Talk] will be misunderstood as [casual talk]. Therefore, the extremely valuable [supplement] is often despised because of this misunderstanding. Recently, most of the [supplements] in many newspapers, in addition to the words and chapters of singing the wind and playing with the moon, are the texts of talking about demons and saying strange things; getting worse and worse, even sperm, genitals, farts, urine, and feces... are taken as important [themes]: Therefore, the most infamous [newspaper ass] has also become its [honorable title]; this is the [supplement's] own inadvertent [speech] and self-inflicted humiliation! Free Talk in the past really contained the tendency of [casual talk]; that is, in recent times, except for Tao Zhiqing's No Chuting Caozhai husband's talk collection and Cheng Zhanlu's Two One Branch Tan, which have lively and profound strokes and the style of [talking about subtle points], almost always found articles that only have literary value but lack the meaning of [praising or criticizing, distinguishing good from evil]. This is naturally the [supernatural] disease of the [no politics] of the previous [supplement]; at the same time, it is also the result of [no freedom] of speech. Once there is [freedom] of speech, even if the [supplement] is small, why can't you talk about national affairs? Because you can't [talk], so [talking] is also [not free]; finally, it's simply [not talking]! Free Talk has to focus on the [talk] aspect. Now I have decided to [transform] from September 1st, this [removing the old and renewing] [advance] is worthy of admiration! I sincerely hope that Free Talk can hold on to an indomitable spirit and stand on the position of [freedom] of speech to say a few more words for the [liberation] and [freedom] of the Chinese people, and even all mankind, after the [transformation] of [September 1st]! I wish:

[[Before [September 1st], [After [September 1st],

Free Talk; Free Talk;

Free Talk, Free Talk,

Free [Talk] Talk. Talk [Freedom]!]]

Poetic Autumn

— Qian Taisheng

Who Can Control Hot Soup and Hot Water?

It's getting cooler in autumn, and the wind is blowing so coolly in people's hearts and minds. Feeling the heat of summer, one cannot help but feel the loveliness of autumn. Summer is so hot that it makes people look for soda and shaved ice. The rotating fan spins overhead, and the cold water cools the whole room, but still, it is嫌着 the heat of summer!

Who can control the three eastern provinces? Those with guns and cannons still can't conquer them, so who will take care of this idle business! Who has forgotten the three northeastern provinces, and needs to be busy with sweat all over in the explosive weather?

Returning from the eastern dawn dance hall, or sleepily emerging from the cinema in the middle of the night, who can get rid of and grab the shadow of the northeast in the atmosphere of flesh in the city?

The autumn wind is coming, after all, it is a poetic autumn. The leaves are rustling, the long wind sweeps the ground, feeling the coolness of autumn, the hot summer is actually forgotten!

The battle situation of January 28 is the time when it can be greatly appreciated. On the banks of the Wusong River, re-boarding the fort, pointing, this is the crater of the bomb thrown by the enemy army, this is the scar of the cannonball fired by the enemy army when twenty-four warships besieged the fort. What an amazing battle record! What a strong poetic meaning, this autumn, this cool autumn!

The northeast has been sinking for years, and the border province of Jehol, the enemy army is attacking again with heavy troops. Jehol, Jehol, who can control this hot soup and hot water? Fortunately, everyone can endure watching the northeast sink for years, and the mere Jehol, who will cheer up?

The Fly in the Beer

— Mian Mian

How the French See Chinese People

The Japanese insulting the Chinese doesn't need me to say. Americans insulting the Chinese in films is also common knowledge. As for the French, they are now on the world stage colluding with the Japanese, so naturally they don't harbor any good feelings towards the Chinese. We can understand the situation by looking at the example given below.

There is a section in a French book with the title [The Fly in the Beer]. Translated as follows:

[When a customer orders a beer in a tavern and finds a fly in the glass, the attitude they take varies depending on their nationality.

The Spaniard pays the money and runs out of the store.

The Frenchman first catches the fly, steps on it to death, and then gives the store staff a loud scolding.

The Englishman spills the beer on the ground and shouts, "Waiter, bring me another glass!" and immediately changes the subject.

The German takes the fly out and drinks the beer again.

The Russian doesn't care about these small things and swallows the fly and the beer together.

Finally, what about the Chinese? He first chews the fly like an experienced gourmet to savor its taste, and then slowly drinks the beer.]

Are there such absurd and outrageous words? Even the Chinese themselves have probably never seen such a Chinese person! A Chinese person who eats flies. I only know that there is a Japanese person who eats caterpillars and snakes. This Japanese person would definitely eat flies as well. But I have never known a Chinese person who eats flies. This is not to save face for the Chinese, but there really is no such talent. The Chinese person in this description is definitely not a real Chinese person living in this world. It must be the Chinese person in the minds of the French.

This description only tells us which countries the French hate. They hate the Germans, Russians, and Chinese. Yes, it is consistent with the current French attitude towards international affairs, isn't it?

Random Thoughts After Waking Up

— Ji Xiang

The Sins of New and Old Sexual Concepts

In this era, everything is contradictory. The old is shaking and collapsing, but its remnants are still left everywhere; the new, waiting to be installed, cannot be installed, and in the end, only some breath is attached.

The old is repelling the new, and the new is cursing the old. It's a pity they don't have a chance to shake hands.

The era is like an enlarged bound foot. The foot binding cloth is removed, and the shoes are enlarged, but its toes are still curved. Walking is unnatural, and sometimes you have to stuff a large piece of cotton into the toe of the shoe.

XXXX

The concepts of the two sexes are always so wonderfully incredible.

I believe that my heart is very frank and pure, without any obscene concepts mixed in it. But when I talk to a woman, I can't help but feel that she is a woman. If this woman is a little prettier, I can still feel a slight intoxication, although I don't think so.

Friend, you probably have this experience too.

XXXX

Regarding the sins of sex, men are generally responsible, which seems to be a matter of course and beyond reproach.

However, scarlet lips, snow-white cheeks, watery charming eyes, annoying fragrance, tight clothes, fleshy stockings, pink trousers: these, these, are everywhere emitting a kind of seductive power. As a result, men pursue and commit crimes.

Is it the man's fault, or is the woman deceiving the man?

Silver Threads

— Jiang Hongjiao

(1)

This small town has been tidied up for more than two months, but the war-torn mounds can still be seen everywhere, although it suffered the least artillery fire and the lightest trampling by the enemy among the many war zones.

However, Ms. Yu Fenruo's home has been destroyed by artillery fire. Apart from a clothing bag that she took with her when she fled the town, she has nothing left. Originally, she was alone, without a husband, children, or any family members. After the war, there was no need to live in this small town again; but she still cared about a madwoman in her neighborhood. Her charitable heart drove her to find this poor woman who was hated by the whole town. She actually found her and lived with her in a house.

Strange! The house where this madwoman lived was only separated from Yu Fenruo's house by a storefront, but it was not bombed by enemy artillery fire, while the neighbors on the left and right had walls collapsed and houses overturned. This madwoman did not escape, and she did not die in the bullets and artillery fire.

This madwoman is too pitiful. She is also alone, without any relatives or family members. Perhaps she has some relatives, but when she is mad, she is very annoying, so no one wants to associate with her, although she also has times when she is mentally clear and not completely mad. Only Yu Fenruo pities her and wants to befriend her, and takes good care of her.

Their lives are very pitiful. Yu Fenruo takes some embroidery work from the embroidery shop in Shanghai to do needlework to make a living. When the madwoman is mentally clear, she carries a cloth basket and mends for people. Yu Fenruo only knows that her surname is Yuan, and she knows nothing about her background and how she became a madwoman; she sometimes asked Yuan, but she never spoke clearly. She only heard her crazy talk when she was mad and vaguely understood that she was a woman who had been abandoned. The people in the town also don't know Yu Fenruo's history, they only know that she is a middle-aged woman, because she is already a forty-year-old woman, and no bad people dare to bully her anymore. She lives a hard life and helps Yuan, who is about the same age as her, to live a pitiful life.

Such women are common in townships and are not surprising, so no one pays attention to them, but an old man from the embroidery shop [release life] (the person who distributes and collects embroidery work to the workers' homes is called release life) looks up to Yu Fenruo and knows that she often helps Yuan. This release life person is called Mr. Wang.

▲Finally Rises by Four Liang One Qian Yesterday's situation of gold standard funds was still chaotic and changing rapidly. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Facing National Crisis Together

— Fo

In my comments on ceasing civil war on August 3rd, I already stated that our country is vast and rich, but there are too many people with leadership ambitions. The only hope is for current military and political leaders to reduce their desire for leadership and instead take a practical, down-to-earth approach. Those capable of unifying a province should start by organizing one province. Those capable of unifying several provinces should start by organizing those provinces. Gain an inch, then another, and start from the beginning. Eventually, there will be a day of unification.

The other day, Mr. Wang Jingwei, in a speech commemorating the week at the Central Party Headquarters, discussed the Rehe problem and methods for facing the national crisis together. He proposed seeking unification through construction and joint governance through balanced power, which aligns with this idea. The only difference is that my construction proposal stemmed from the cessation of civil war, while Mr. Wang's proposal was for facing the national crisis together. If ceasing civil war, this proposal is a good remedy for the illness. If facing the national crisis together, releasing this proposal is like ["a slow doctor encountering a sudden wind"], truly as if the whip cannot reach the horse's belly.

Mr. Wang's three methods are: First, the provinces that can be unified should have their difficulties resolved and be actively reorganized and built up, so that the people can live in peace and prosperity. In these provinces, set up a model of modern politics. Second, the provinces that nominally obey the Central Government but are not fully consistent should plan for unification through construction. Third, organize the people. These are all methods for organizing internal affairs during peacetime and not methods for jointly facing the national crisis, because these methods will definitely not be effective in one or two years. Distant water cannot put out a nearby fire.

Now, the national crisis is at hand, like a fire burning one's eyebrows. If we continue to leisurely reorganize the internal affairs, the national crisis will become reality, and there will be no hope of saving it. Therefore, my proposal is only ["I would rather be a shattered jade than an intact tile"], which is what Mr. Wang called ["If there is a gun or a bullet, we must resist to the death"]. No matter what the sacrifice, we must make the enemy pay a corresponding price. If our country has such an army, our people will do their utmost to assist. Ma Zhanshan, the 19th Route Army, and the 5th Army are examples.

Art and Literature

Autumn Night Thoughts

— Yi Seng

(1)

The bleak autumn wind and autumn rain, pitiful are the lands of Heilongjiang and Jilin. The Tartar tries to restore his country, but first loses it. The Jianzi garrison the border, but ultimately abandon it. The righteous soldiers struggle with the will to restore, the central court offers only lip service to resist. Don't lightly speak of the national crisis as an ordinary matter, only a few years have passed since the loss of Keelung and Taiwan.

(2)

Suddenly comes news of the generals and ministers evasive, the colors of the skies shift in the northern and southern capitals. Competing in emotion rather than facing foreign insults, unable to balance, the center is lost. The people of the East Province have sunk into a new country, the bandits of the Red Province have burdened the old corners. In such a country, in such a night, why cherish one's worthless head?

Science

Pine Needle Cotton Manufacturing Method

— Jiang Tianlan

For artificial cotton, we only know about using rice straw, but we don't know that pine needles are also the only raw material for making cotton. Moreover, pine needles are cheaper than rice straw, and the profit is greater after making cotton. Anyone who cares about industry may wish to study pine needle cotton production.

However, the pine needle cotton manufacturing method that I know is to take old and strong pine needles, dry them in the sun, and then soak them in hot water at 60 degrees Celsius for about six hours. Take them out and add 1 part of water, 1 part of alcohol, and 1/5 part of yeast, mixing them well. Take a wooden board with several small holes, put a bamboo mat underneath, and add stones on top to press the pine needles down, so that they do not float on the surface of the water.

There should be holes in the cylinder cover to allow air to circulate. Then, fermentation gradually begins inside the cylinder, increasing the heat. The length of soaking depends on the warmness or coldness of the weather. Generally, it will foam in about two weeks. When the fermentation has reached the appropriate level, the wooden plug at the bottom of the cylinder can be pulled out to release the alkaline water. If there is still glue or oil in the leaves that does not dissolve in water, add a thin potassium hydroxide solution and mix it together, then introduce steam, the glue or oil will dissolve and flow out with the water. Wash with water and steam several times, and then let it dry appropriately.

At this time, if the skin cannot be completely removed, it can be placed in a round sieve and rotated quickly to separate the skin. Then, apply the final procedure to make it soft, place it in a mortar or on a flat board, cover it with coarse cloth, and pound it with a stick, then rub it finely through a sieve. The resulting fibrous material is pure cotton. The chips sifted out can be burned to make a kind of pine soot.

I am just broadly describing this method based on what I know, for experimental purposes. There is no shortage of inventors in the world, and there should be more detailed methods than this one. I am writing to ask for instruction.

Social Improvement Discussion Group

Should Mid- and Lower-Class Funeral Homes Be Established?

— Zong Bai

Weddings and funerals are events that everyone experiences. However, most of society is made up of middle and lower-class people. The homes of middle-class people are usually just barely adequate. Sometimes two families share a residence, or even three. It goes without saying the homes of lower-class people are worse, and several people live in one room with a kitchen or a three-tiered shelf. When a celebratory event comes, one can borrow a restaurant or hotel. There are different levels for middle-class and lower-class people, but this does not need mentioning.

But when a funeral occurs, a big problem arises. If someone is about to die, the landlord will not allow them to die in the house, and the co-residents also dislike it. Sending them to the hospital, the doctor says there is no way to save their life, and the hospital cannot accept them. At that time, there is truly nowhere to go. One can only let them die in the street and then not know where to grab a place to collect the corpse and hold the funeral. Do you think middle and lower-class people suffer at this time? Not to mention lower-class people. Even for middle-class people, if they can die at home, and hold a funeral in a single-story house, there is no place to entertain relatives and friends who come to pay their respects. They inevitably have to use the alley outside the house, set up a bamboo shed, and put out some mismatched tables and chairs to entertain them. This is all without any way to think about it. If the weather is hot, with the sun at 100-some degrees, it is impossible to sit under the bamboo shed. If the weather is cold, with wind blowing from both sides, it is also impossible to sit. So, I think that funeral homes for the middle and lower classes should be established.

In Shanghai, there is a magnificent Wanguo Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road, but it is only for the enjoyment of the upper class. Glass coffins, various ways to preserve the corpse, all kinds of expenses, it costs at least one or two thousand taels to move a hand. Lower-class people should not even talk about it. Middle-class people can only sigh with admiration. Therefore, middle and lower-class funeral homes should be planned for early. Everyone can imitate the methods of the Wanguo Funeral Home and treat it as a business organization. Shanghai is such a large place, with such a large population, that three or five funeral homes can be accommodated. Perhaps many people think that doing upper-class funerals can bring more profit. But the majority of society is made up of middle and lower-class people. If you take small profits but sell a lot, isn't it a good business? Moreover, these kinds of funeral homes don't require much capital. You only need to rent a house, the smaller one can be a double-story house, and the bigger one can be three-up and three-down. Use one or two employees, and don't decorate too lavishly. The way to make money is to charge rent to the bereaved family for renting the rooms, and to take a fair commission on the coffin and ceremonial arrangements. Wouldn't that be a good business? This is an easy undertaking, which is very beneficial to the lives of the people and the society. Why doesn't everyone try to start one? (For Discussion)

Dark Side

Returning Disappointed

— Flood

In this society where all industries are declining and there is economic panic, groups of people are wandering at crossroads, struggling with their lives. They want to find a job to make a living, but the shadow of ["few monks and much porridge"] is always flashing before your eyes. But what can be done?

Mr. Huang was fortunate enough to enter a certain cultural organization, filling a small clerical position. As far as I know, he receives a monthly salary of 30 yuan, and must provide his own room and board. Also, he must bear all of his family's expenses. In the family, there is a wife, a three-month-old baby, and a mother over half a century old, and they are all unable to produce. It is very obvious that it is difficult to maintain such a family with such income.

Because of the heavy pressure of life, his body became weaker day by day. Due to the harsh environment, it affected his willpower. He felt that everything from now on seemed to be drifting in a fog. He saw a group of sinister faces smiling maliciously at him, but he could not think of a way to deal with them. He had a way, but he did not have the courage to do it. One morning, Mr. Huang was reading the newspaper advertisements, and unconsciously saw an advertisement for a typing school, how low the tuition was, how useful it was to graduate... Mr. Huang's heart moved, and he smiled at the newspaper. As a result, he pawned a sheepskin robe and registered at a certain typing school because he wanted to gain a skill that could help him in life.

In that small Western-style pavilion, with four typewriters and a light bulb, was all the property of the school. A well-dressed teacher came to meet him and began to talk to Mr. Huang.

["Are you here to learn typing? Uh, your honorable name?"] The teacher looked up and asked.

["I am here to learn typing, I am called Huang Baiman, may I ask your honorable name, who is your principal?"]

["My last name is Zhu, I run this school. Now I want to talk briefly with Mr. Huang. The school course is divided into three classes: intensive, special, and ordinary. The intensive course can be graduated in one month, the special course in two months, and the ordinary course in three months. Once practiced, you can type with your eyes closed. Every graduate of this school is introduced into a company or bank... The salaries are quite large. Which class does Mr. Huang want to join?"] Principal Zhu asked, smiling from ear to ear.

["Intensive class!"] Mr. Huang blurted out. He thought to himself, although the school building has only one pavilion, judging from what Principal Zhu just said, the achievements in society are quite good, and the salaries of the students introduced are said to be quite large. At this time, Mr. Huang's mind was filled with the four words "great hope."

["Then, please pay the registration fee first! Two dollars, you can come to school tomorrow, and then pay the tuition of thirteen yuan, and the paper and supplies fee of two yuan. The registration fee is deducted from the tuition. If you don't come, it will not be refunded. The time is at your convenience, from 9:00 a.m. to 9:00 p.m."] Principal Zhu seemed to show a look of accommodating the students.

Three days later, Mr. Huang's tuition was already being forced to death by Principal Zhu. When he was practicing typing, Principal Zhu taught him with a disdainful look. So Mr. Huang used nine oxen and two tigers to barely pay the tuition in full. He thought that if he did not pay it off quickly, Principal Zhu would definitely see that he was a poor man, and he would definitely get a great obstacle, so it is better to please him early. However, the fact was exactly the opposite. After paying the tuition, this Principal Zhu always hid in his wife's room, singing the "Sister!... " tune very vigorously, as if Mr. Huang bought a ticket to listen to the opera. He did not give any guidance on typing methods, etc. Instead, when the time was about to come, Principal Zhu dragged his light leather shoes to the classroom to prepare to turn off the lights.

The graduation period arrived, and Principal Zhu routinely issued so-called graduation diplomas to the students, and naturally Mr. Huang was also given this grace.

["Huang Baiman, I will notify you when there is an opportunity, goodbye, goodbye!"]

["……………"]

On the way home, Mr. Huang sighed deeply. Not only was it not quick, but what is the use of taking a ready-made graduation diploma that can be bought for five cents in a bookstore? Not to mention having to fill in a one-yuan stamp himself? The expectation of helping in life is still in the deep clouds.

A Corner of Society

Page 23

The Birthday of the Three Officials

— Yuechan

["Sister-in-law Huang, is today the 27th day of the seventh lunar month, the birthday of the Three Officials?" (sound inversion)], a middle-aged woman said to her cohabitant, a young woman holding a child.

["That's right, I forgot. I wanted to buy a foot tub because the one I bought last year for the Three Officials' birthday has rotted like tofu. Auntie Wu, are you going to buy anything?" Sister-in-law Huang said with a smile. ["Yes! My rice steamer is broken. I wanted to buy one on the 27th day of the first month (there are three 27th days in a year: the first, seventh, and tenth months), but I knew the celebrations were cancelled because of the war. I thought I'd buy one today, maybe it'll be cheaper, so I've waited until now. Let's go!"] Auntie Wu, always impatient, urged them on as usual.

["Oh dear! Why are you in such a hurry? Thank you, can you wait a moment?"]

["Then hurry up"]…

In a short while, Auntie Wu and Sister-in-law Huang, leading her four-year-old child, Sannan, left the shikumen and headed towards Lujiabang Road.

XXXXXXXX

Lujiabang Road in the Nanshi district, usually deserted, has been bustling with vendors these past few days, eager to do business. As a result, it has gradually become lively. Furniture, silk stockings, bamboo and rattan ware – all unsellable leftovers from the year – are being sold. They employ various methods to attract customers: ringing bells, striking their wares, shouting at the top of their voices, and even using peep shows with puppet shows, enticing people with the clanging of gongs and drums. It's a noisy and bustling scene.

["Mommy! I want to see the peep show!"] Sannan pleaded with her mother, Sister-in-law Huang.

["No, we didn't bring enough money,"] she said, putting on her motherly air, giving a reason why she couldn't let her watch.

Sannan knew her hopes for fun today were dashed, so she had to obediently follow them.

After all, people are never satisfied, especially women. They buy this and then want to buy that, and even if they already have it at home, they want to buy it again. They only cared about the cheap prices and didn't care about the quality of the goods. They bought over a dozen items in total, so many that they couldn't carry them all in their four hands. They had to hire a rickshaw. They let the rickshaw puller overcharge them by a dime or two. When they got home and thought about it carefully, they realized there was no real bargain. On the contrary, they had spent three or four dimes more on the rickshaw fare. They really felt it wasn't worth it.

Alas!

Love and Bread

— Yiping

The sky was not yet light, and the entire N village was immersed in sweet dreams. Two blurry figures suddenly emerged from the stone bridge at the pier, running quickly forward, as if carrying a major mission. The boat bound for Shanghai was docked beside the pier, as if waiting just for them. As soon as they boarded, it set off. Inside the boat, a dim oil lamp was lit, distinguishing them as a man and a woman. Their faces were flushed, and their chests were still heaving. They occupied a corner of the cabin. They smiled at each other, leaned on each other, and fell into a deep sleep.

At noon that day, N village was in an uproar about the elopement of a certain local gentry's daughter and the son of a grocery store owner; but the two of them said that free love had triumphed, and they had safely arrived in Shanghai.

Those who have been in the river of love naturally understand that this is the most difficult moment to describe in life. In the big hotels and dance halls of the city: : in all areas of sin, they lived a romantic, carnal life. But this money pit quickly used up all the money they had stolen. It was only then that they realized that love was as important as bread. They moved from a big hotel into a small attic room, from a life of revelry to seeing the faces of rich friends. Money only goes out and doesn't come in. They felt slightly disappointed. By chance, they saw a classified advertisement for a secretarial position with a monthly salary of thirty yuan. He solemnly picked up his pen and wrote a few lines of regular script neatly for the first time, attached a detailed address, and mailed it out with great hope. That night, they thought they had found a new life, and they prepared some drinks and snacks in a very ["miserable"] (not abundant) way, encouraging them to forget their past disappointments and celebrate their future success. They spent a relatively pleasant evening like this.

When they woke up in the morning, from the next day onwards, they waited for a reply. But one day, two days… until they couldn't pay the second month's rent, and after they were disappointed again, they realized that bread was more important than love. On the one hand, they pawned things to make ends meet, and on the other hand, they were at a loss. They tried to find opportunities in the newspaper and discovered that a certain publishing house was soliciting manuscripts for a special issue of unknown writers. He thought he should work hard in this area. When he was in school before, he had served as the editor of the school magazine. He happily told her about this idea, and that night, he wrote a manuscript of ten thousand words. The next day, when the sun came up, he still didn't feel tired.

The special issue of unknown writers was finally published. They spent five dimes to buy it and saw that it was full of works by top writers in Shanghai. At the end, there was a submitted manuscript, and the editor's note said that the space was limited and could not include too much, and hoped that the unknown writers would continue to work hard, and that their publication was absolutely open.

He tore the book to pieces and remembered that she had said she was going to borrow money from a classmate's house and had not returned for three nights. He sighed deeply, ["Life is for bread, and doesn't need love"].
